O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	To you, dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine together with its content, and I have brought it to an end by its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is corrupted in our region and is alien to everything everywhere, the science and art are destroyed, and nothing remains of it but small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this (dislocation), errors and vanities have arisen, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is dismissed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will describe the process of this treatise together with its arrangement according to the way of exposition and declaration, and abbreviation; and I will also come together with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of work accompanied by the explanation and preparation for their use as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands in our time, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes [this task] should be knowledgeable in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to know the judgment of limbs, their shapes and connections and separations thereof, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and marrow, and the number of joints, and the moving and resting veins and the reposing ones, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates said that the hand with the thumb is not much, but with work it is enough; and similarly in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We advise you in the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the matters previously mentioned, be careful not to make mistakes and not to operate on people; thus, I have seen many who engage in this science and abandon both their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut open one abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; therefore so much blood came out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another man who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; he carried away a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within 4 days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for him to extract it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if he cut it he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And there was another man who took care of a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breakage he had an open wound; and the ignorant man pulled the broken part over the wound with great force, and did not leave any skin at the wound, and left it in that state; and he commanded that it should not be released; and it remained like this until the leg became completely swollen and the toes and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him and hurried to release the leg; and when I released it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and he could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire member was destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And (there is) another mirror which will cause an abscess to collapse, and then inflame it due to the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when the chancre is pure of black bile, it should not be touched by iron if it is not in its place where everything corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two categories: one in which there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show you in each section of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary for you to protect yourself so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Take your weapons in custody, and approach your patients gently yet firmly, and use the best way so by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave aside diseases of despairing health; and remove your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of bad diseases, lest you be called a foolish person."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have designed this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and cold medicine cauteries, and the chapters are arranged from head to feet; and the forms of instruments, and iron implements for cautery, and everything that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about ventouses (sucking cups) and wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are arranged and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell the quality of aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are lengthy and subtle words and secret responses, and many wise people spoke about it, and they agreed with this; however, their words were not enough for me because I will shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally with every complexion where there is matter, whether it be two complexions: namely, the hot complexion with matter, and the dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry conditions, some said that the fire cautery is great aid; while others said the opposite: that the fire cautery is not beneficial for illness caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure hot illnesses by heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite stated that the fire cautery provides great aid for hot and dry illnesses that come from human bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body and its moisture in relation to the nature of fire, you will find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, let no one interfere except those who have tested it and who know through long practice the chapter of cauterizations, and the variety of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and duration of time; we do not fear others' complexions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the sick will conform to and agree with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery combined with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it affects only the member that is burned, and harms no other member unless by name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another through transmission, and bring great illnesses of difficult healing to the affected member; and by chance, they may kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its strength and the goodness of its substance, does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this for you by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is true concerning things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of the words, because I do not like to withhold from you the secret which is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstration; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on when the cauteries should be done, and chose companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is fitting in all times, because the harm occurring below is aided by the cautery; and likewise, if the cauteries are for necessary pain other than one that can wait for a time when greater damage will not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about it, dear child, as foolish people do; because a sickness cured by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because cauteries are not medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors which cause pain, and is more effective than medicine due to the speed of its action, and because of the virtue of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And sometimes the illness comes according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its power; and superfluidities are gathered in him through the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in that place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as with cauterization for pain, and similar things; and the pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the rear of medicine, and this is to see; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth more than medicine after it, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clearly stated that cauteries are at the rear of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish healers.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cauteries were melted rather than iron ones, and they spoke untruthfully because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the head of a cautery does not cause pus, but this is not true because I have tested it, and found that it is true in some cases; and gold cauteries are more effective than iron ones, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know if it is heated by the color of the gold, and it may sometimes cool down; and if you heat it too much, it will burn; thus there are enough obstacles to this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore, we use fire cautery which has been adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered you this chapter about the head from neck to feet, because the veins are easier to find in this way.
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for both moist and cold conditions of the brain, and it is used due to a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and because of numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a medicinal solution, cleansing the head four times or twice, depending on what the properties and age and custom of the patient can endure; and then, after the head of the patient, proceed.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on a soft surface; afterward, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes; and where your thumb will come, it will bleed slightly, then heat the cautery called "olivare", which is its shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the swollen area marked with ink, and make a downward and pulling motion with your thumb and thumb, slowly turning it; then remove your thumb immediately, and return the area if you see the bone slightly protruding; and if you do not see it, continue to apply the cautery as I told you until you see the bone; afterwards, take a small amount of fat, put it in soft cotton and place it on the area, leave it for three days; afterwards, place moistened linen on it; and leave it until the burn is healed; afterwards, treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as the ancients said, when a wound remains open longer, it drains more; and for this reason, if it is covered, it heals faster.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that the fire cautery should burn part of the bone, and then heal the one who is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery should be burned above, and push so hard that it depresses the bone as much as a walnut shell, because women use these to expel fluids from their wounds; afterwards, one must let the wound remain open for a long time, and then heal and cure.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two kinds of cauteries do not seem good to me altogether, except in some men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head becomes weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other members; and likewise when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more effective to me, and from this use I work with assurance for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic and long-lasting pain in the head, the patient should use wormwood and pills called "cochie", and of purges for the head and oils and plasters; and if they do the cautery that we have said before, it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is strong in nature and not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and perform one cautery called "vasselz"; it is one place where ventouses are placed; hold your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later; and the cauterizations of the horns should be subtler than those with which the middle part of the head is cauterized, and here is its shape:
dou cautere dou chief	head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the disease extends to the eye, and the head is purged with universal medicines, and other treatments have been performed as I said in the division of diseases, and nothing helps; then cauteries are applied according to two methods: medicine of cold and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of the cold medicine is that you take a hot coal and peel off its bark, place one piece on each of the two heads (eyes), then make an incision where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the hot coal under the skin; when it has been placed, press and hold it firmly for twelve hours; then release and treat the coal with vinegar and leave the wound for two or three days; afterwards cover it with linen soaked in butter.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment until it is healed; and if you see that this does not work, use one of the medications I have written or treat with the twelfth treatment of combustive medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The cautery of fire is as follows. Heat the cauterizer according to this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the tip resembles a keyhole with one inch of curvature and a small appearance; place it on the painful area, hold your hand steady, and slightly touch the iron, allowing the middle part of the iron to burn until half its thickness is burnt; remove your hand from the fire so that only the artery does not burn, and let blood flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in alum water, place it on the area for four days; then put damp cotton in butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this inflammation with the cautery called "cultellare", prick it at the tip, but be careful not to cut the artery in this inflammation which is not old.
de emigraine	From migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraine, as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that fire cauteries as mentioned before in medicine and iron do not help, then you must heat the cautere called "cultellare" until it is white; and hold steady on the spot a line of half a finger's length, and press your hand once, and hold so as not to hit the artery or reach the bone; beware of the jaw that becomes motionless when eating, and let nerves have no regard but for the motionless one and for spasms not to come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or when cutting it there should be great fear, especially in those who do not know it and are not experienced; leave the operation in progress; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals. If you find a vein, administer the cautere mentioned earlier or in the chapter of artery extraction with a cautere having two blades; this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears on one side due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from coldness and it has been treated with medicinal remedies and other cures as we have said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poins," which is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After heating the entire ear around the sick area, or in both places where the pain is located, move away from the root of the ear about an inch since you have identified its location; and have 10 heated cauteries around each ear; after healing the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torment that should be cured by cautery is not other than those that move due to phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not perform cauterization on similar things that come from scab or nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torment that moves due to phlegm from eyes and purges of the head and gargarism, it is not worthwhile, therefore you must cauterize the patient with four cauteries: one in the root of the ear, another a little way beyond the temple, and the third on the cheekbone; place the cautery in the open healthy part, and make it cauterize towards the top of the ear a little below the horn, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery in place until half of the charcoal is burned; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance of the surgeon's instrument we have mentioned is similar, but it is slightly more subtle and the knife should be a little larger; after curing the wound as I have previously said, let it remain clean when it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not benefit, and the patient does not have fever, then administer four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the head itself, and one at the site called "basin" as we have previously said, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; let them be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	diarrhea (in Old French)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large ears and round pills filled with cerebrum; afterwards, anoint the head of the patient completely, and place the plaster of mustard (sinapi) on the occiput which is written or treated as plasters; and this is the method for cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in this way, it is good; if not, make four cauteries of oil on the head from neck to collar, with two spaces between each cautery and one inch wide; and cure it as others, and if you see it is needed and the patient is enduring, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, another two on the two horns, and cure it until it is healthy; and may the cauteries called "olive oil" be like I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chill of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is required that the head be cleansed with years and what was said before; after washing the patient's head, then make a fire cautery on the patient's head and on each horn, and one behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; leave it until the deeper part is burned, lift your hand; after healing it, let it become healthy again, and heal the cautery that is called "olivare" as was said before.
de l’epilempsie	In addition to what has been said previously, for epilepsy:
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For epilepsy, the use of a fire cautery should only be used for those who are suffering from inflammation, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain with years and other cures as was said in the division when the patient is large and suffering from thinking about medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, give him gargling and frequent chewing of the cereal, softening it with good foods; afterward place the head on a cushion, and make one cautery as we have said before, and one cautery on the navel, and one on each horn; and if the patient is outside and enduring, make cauteries as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spinal cord of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are superfluidities or corrupted and thick phlegm, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said for him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then you should give him to drink something that purifies the brain, according to what was mentioned earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, take the patient's head; afterwards make a linen bandage, like a circle, place it around his head; cross the patient, and keep him tightly bound on all sides; then apply the liniment, which is made of old cow butter; heat it gently so that it can be poured without causing discomfort; after emptying the circle inside the head, let it cool; do this to the patient once a week with good governance until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to perform cauterization, make many more points on the entire cautery. This method of cauterization strengthens the brain greatly; and then place dampened cotton soaked in butter and linseed oil on top.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the water comes first to the eyes with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then start and give the patient something purifying the head, and keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more than once while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, command him to lower his head, and make a fire cautery on the head, and make two cauterizations on the temples where the discharge of water is in both eyes or one eye; and burn all the veins and arteries beneath the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for the discharge of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with your power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and the incision the caution as to how you will stop it; and sometimes a fire cautery or hatereil is done beneath the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	The body weeps tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	If the eyes are old and accustomed to weep and they are above the veins or along the arteries that appear on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is due to cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cautery I said at the beginning of this work for the eyelids: namely, a cautery for the forehead, two cauteries above the temples, two cauteries or scissors under the eyebrows; and if necessary, cauterize it carefully below the eyelid.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The body weeps tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it is of no benefit, then give the sick person three cups of warm wine; after this, burn the chief and make a cautery or olive oil cautery; also make two cauteries called "clavilis" on top of the two sores, one under the hair; and beware of the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then make this cautery called "olive oil". Here is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to perform two cauterizations on the two witches, as long as they are; and do not leave your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the oils are converted into a piercing state and prick oil, and then cauterization is performed according to two methods: either with fire, or with a burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are grown and even, then put the patient in a safe position; next, on top of the hairs, draw a figure that is like the fennel seed pod, and make the start of the sign to be at the base of the hairs; then put moistened cotton soaked with egg white and musk oil on the oil, then heat the cautery in the shape described:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize on the figure you have drawn multiple times, so that the hairs are burned in that spot; and the signs of the healing of the work are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs raised at the point of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter so that the burn is removed; afterwards, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if later the hairs grow and the skin becomes soft, then resume the fire cautery on that same spot as you did before; and if the hairs curl, cauterize until the skin rises to its natural level, is even, and does not prick the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal hot cautery is to instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then take parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; next take French soap and hot iron, each one .З., and grind them together well; make it quickly so it does not cool, spread it over the parchment as with the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin; if the patient holds oil in only one spot, you should work only on that one spot, and if on both spots; put cotton soaked in egg white beneath the oil; and the patient's joint should be healthy, and hold your hand showing over the medicine, and press a little pouch and move it all the times when the patient feels the burning sensation of the medicine, for he will feel burning sensations as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the bite has passed, lift up the affected limb and examine if it rises in the same way as when it was raised by fire or incision; and if it does so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the limb, or if no medicine has worked yet, continue with your treatments until they are even, and place the fingers at their correct positions; then place cotton moistened in butter over the burned area until the blisters have healed, then treat the limb with a salve called "dyafenis" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful with your treatment because the medicine is pricking at the eyes, and if the skin becomes soft after that, and the hairs start to prick in the oil, then repeat the medicine on that limb which has been properly cleaned as before; afterwards treat it until it heals; this is the form of the mirte leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the human hair is of various sizes and according to this, your treatments should be adjusted; do not deviate from the correct path for those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating a fistula as we have said in the description of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in a basin or shallow dish filled with warm water; then take a piece of wool soaked in egg white or linen dipped in oil and lay it over the fistula; after that, heat the cautery to a red-hot state like the tip of a bird's feather, pointed from one end to the other, but it should also be round if necessary.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, remove the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, remove the worms; afterwards place the hot cautery on it, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the nail to avoid burns; and place the cautery in the oil fat, and rot it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you begin the cautery up to the bone, it would be good. If not, start again with the cautery once more, and another if needed, and let it rest for three days; afterwards put soft cotton soaked in butter on it, and the ointment drying treatment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king according to what he writes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And here is a method of cauterizing a fistula that the ancients did not say. Understand a fistula, and split the side of it; afterwards put one subtle camphor capsule in the incision:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make the quantity of a .Z. of plug; hold your hand firmly and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not spill onto him; and it is necessary that you place oil on top of the patient's cotton soaked in egg or awen: the plug will direct the flow of the fistula, and the healthy part heals marvelously through wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good. If not, it is necessary to administer fumigation to the chest and bring the fistula back into the chest as appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cavities occur in lips, which are called "hair-like", and equally in children's lips.

de l’aposteme de la goule	Of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes pus-filled and swollen and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help at all: then you must have one cautery according to the size of the fistula; after draining or opening the fistula, keep your hand until the iron feels hot at its tip and where it was placed; and do this once or twice, after treating what we have said about treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed in this way, it is good; but if not, you must find the location and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the teeth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums become soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but that is of no use, then put the head of the patient in hot water; after scalding the cautery as the method will come later, place a cane on the tooth; and put the hot cautery into it quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after releasing your hand and repeating the cautery according to your wish; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with saltwater, and keep it there for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving teeth are stabilized, the softened gums are kept in place, and the corrupting moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the tooth comes from cold or there is either cold or worm, and the medicines have no effect, then it will require cauterization according to two methods: cauterization with a lancet and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and moisten it with hot butter, and place it on the painful tooth as quickly as possible and hold it until it becomes cold; and thus do frequently until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the linen and cotton become cooled in cold butter, then place it on the tooth again, and put a hot iron above it until the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The cautery with fire is such that you take a cane of iron or bronze, and it should be thick so that the heat does not burn the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, after which its form will come out, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this frequently, as the pain will disappear that day or the next. And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then spit it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery for whatever head you wish, and do it according to your ability; this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	for scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofulas are due to cold and damp, and not responsive to medicine for digestion, then heat the fire cautery as follows: make two holes for the smoke to exit from the other side; place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery accordingly with the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days; then put cotton soaked in butter over the blister until the sore is healed. Afterward, cure the affected area with ointments and plasters until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moisture conquers over the channel of the thigh, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should first be purged with soluble medicines; afterwards do cautery at the root of the neck, making sure not to come close to the throat, but only a little. Afterwards, do one more cautery at the joint of the neck and the head of the spine, and let it be the cautery that is called "clavile" because we have described its shape before; heal the wound until it is healed.
de la toust	When the moisture conquers over the thigh channel, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should first be purged with soluble medicines. de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is dislocated above this nerve, for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the cautery, break it with oil and then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until he is comforted.

dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said that one should make cauterizations for pleurisy with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and also as large and as long as your thumb; immerse it in oil, and heat it up, then cauterize one cautery between the ribcage and neck, and two small cauterizations a little lower in the area below the beard; two cauterizations between the fifth and sixth costal cartilage, declining slightly behind a bit; one cautery at the side, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the side affected by the cautionery that is between the shoulders; do not press hard, but perform it as openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And said some ancient one that a man should use a cautery like a razor and heat it up and put it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; then the pain subsides, as we have said in the liver abscess. But in this work there is fear or the patient dies immediately, or fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mice (mouse bite) as we have said in the divisions of treatment, and it does not improve, then there are three ways of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	The first way is that you make four cauteries in a line according to the length of the mouse, following the figure of the liver cautery as we have said before; and do not press too hard with your hand, and let the patient be aware on his back.

And another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the cavity where the mouse is, or the sore that comes towards the left side of the patient, and the elevations you make on the cavity should be according to the body's cavity, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After putting the two inflamed nerves in flame so that the boils are pierced from the other side, and then pull the cautery out, thus there will be four. And if you see, cauterize with the entire cautery on all four nerves. After healing when it has discharged pus for a long time, it is necessary to apply the cure mentioned before.
de ydropisie	From hydropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The cautery is not effective for hydropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes". When you cure it according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the swelling, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the bladder, two behind the back near the spine, and one at the site of pain; and let the cauteries be close to the edge of the boil.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery is opened to expel pus for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will come together with the help of God.

The form of the cautery for the belly is the clavicle as shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it has been stated before.
de l’enfleure des piez	swelling of the feet

de la menoison	of the remedy

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh-like substance called "thelul"

de plaie mal curee	of an ill-healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear incision or opening, we will describe the disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	1. When a fistula comes, and it is swollen and infected with corrupt moisture, you must test it entirely with subtle probing, and be aware that you know the extent of the probe completely.
de la maladie des reins	On the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and with great swelling, and does not take on a female form, then you must make a cautery over the kidneys on both sides with the cautery clavile as we have previously said; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be four cauteries in a row, and they will provide more help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then you make a cautery on the part outside the bladder, where the hairs begin at the tip, one on the right and one on the left, each as long as our thumb; and you make one cautery on the other side of the back if needed, or two if necessary; and the cauteries should be as thick as a nail according to the shape mentioned above.
de la marris	Of the anus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the anus is cold and moist and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term ends slowly; and when they come, it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the anus, as we have said in the treatment of the bladder, and two cauteries on the other side of the back; and the cauteries should be as thick as a nail, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the swelling
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the swelling's container and thus causes it to move out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joint is found to have moved from its proper place, then you must cauterize the patient on the swelling's container with a cautionery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint surrounding the container so that the container is within the circle; and if the cautery is as those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautionery is not present, make four large olive-oil cauteries and let them be as full as all the others; and let it heal until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the swelling of a hernia, and it is due to coldness or moisture, and the patient is cured of this as we have said in the division, but the cure is not worthwhile; and the disease is ancient: therefore you must purge the patient with foul-smelling pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, you perform the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: namely with burning medicines, or cautery by fire. Cautery by fire is according to many methods, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the swelling of a hernia four triangular cauterizations according to this form (shown below), and make a good depth and width, and have space between each cauterization equal to the thickness of a thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautionery is performed in the middle on the head of the hernia, for which there are four according to this form:
