Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, use the round cautery in the circle as we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the shoulder; but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire shoulder, and all the edges should be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method for sciatica when the pain is in the shoulder and does not reach the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and leg, make 2 cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle .4 fingers, on the left side a little; and let the cauteries be made with a lancet, and burn the edges of the wound; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the foot or very close to it, cauterize there where he feels the pain 2 or 4 times using the cautery called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a lancet or circular shape, and be careful in all your cauterizations not to let the cautery burn nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient any greater harm or contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made a fire cautery on the foot of the ankle, and they left it until the entire leg was swollen, and the feet also, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted. After a belly solution in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this method. // The wise men will say in the cautery of the heel, here is how it is done, make a nail like iron rod, about as thick as a little finger, or slightly less, and pass it through both from above to below, with a space the size of a nut, and the distance between the holes should be two fingers apart, and they should be round, and it should have one handle of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heat it so that it becomes completely red and roasted, and then place it on the sick heel box, turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave for four days; then apply a plaster of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery due to its fearsome appearance, and few who use it know how to do so; but nonetheless it is a good cautery which can be borne by those who can endure it, and there where it burns.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, either from falling or striking or excessive evacuation, or from similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these symptoms are worth cauterizing except for one who suffers from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is required afterwards that the patient be emptied of fetid pills or similar things, which are placed on the back, where the pain occurs, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 or more cauteries according to its potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make 4 cauteries or 4 at the mid-sized cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; and you find it in the lower spine of the back and in its appearance which appears above other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The first sentence in the provided Old French text translates to: "The fire cautery increases each part of the spine. If you see it, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing 2 or 3 lines and let the tips be close to each other. After healing, cure the area until it is healed according to what has been said, and take care not to apply a cautery in a gland that contains nerve."
de la dolor des jointes	"of the pain of joints"
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	"When the pain of joints is due to moisture that spreads throughout all parts of the body, and when it comes in feet, which people call gout properly, and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make a small amount of cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:"
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary for you to prick the face of the foot, make a fire cautery all over the cautery which is called "point". And if pain comes up to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, make a fire cautery on each knee four times or four on each part, all over the olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand outside for longer than the fat of the skin is burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If the pain descends to the knees and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pain is in the hands, make punctures around the tendons two lines long; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pain comes up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and think about medicines. For if you take good care of him and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sifac
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When worms come in wounds, and the belly swells as a result, it is necessary that when you wish to treat it, the patient should not eat anything that day; and that he uses things which relieve the stomach, so that the worms descend from his stomach; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm straight until the belly recovers, and then press down on the swelling at your sides, and press firmly on top of the wound over the bone of the elbow, and give a sign that resembles half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery as shown in this figure:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and let the worms come out. Then press down on the worms to their place; and the assistant holds his hand over where they cannot return; and you should work well the patient's thighs, and put one cushion and one sergeant on his thighs, and one other on the side which keeps his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your might, and hold it straight and until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful that the worms do not escape when you perform the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that because of this the patient does not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. It is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and those of large people as large as theirs; after three days cure the wound from the cautery with butter until it is healed; after that cure other medicaments until it is healthy, and make the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his wounds be left open long enough, so that the worms do not escape when he goes to his room.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wishes to rise, bring a well-made bandage for him and keep it for another 40 days; let him have good rest, but let him not overwork or be too filled with drinking and eating, and avoid excessive laughter; and if he follows this teaching, he will recover entirely. And I shall say the cure of cutting in its chapter afterwards.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the hernia from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When hernias appear in other bellies and are recognized as not growing anymore, let one cautery be made according to its size, and it should be burned the third of the skin; afterwards cure as we have said; and no old men have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at four angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first, mark the location and make a line above the wound and another below, and take your hand to hold the entire cautery. However, the initial cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain occurs in any limb, either from falling or being injured, and that pain lasts a long time and the medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the member, its size, its weakness, its virtue, and its location for twisting and its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, repeat another cautery on top of it, because it is customary that it should change in the limb that is closest, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	To mix medications
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Mixtures of medications are sometimes helped by cautery with great care, and particularly those patients who come from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see them to be cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not dissolve nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption will affect the entire patient, then perform five cauteries on the head: one on the forehead at the end of the hair; two on the two horns; one behind the ears; and leave your hand until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out forcefully so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and then cauterize on the cheek according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the medication is scattered everywhere, it clearly perishes, then you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the calf and another below it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the veins that are above the last calcament, that you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more you perform cautery, the more help it provides and benefits the patient; and know that sick people feel no pain during cauterization as healthy ones do, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary that the cautery be large or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron-working. After cure the wound with wheat flour, honey and other treatments until it heals.
de enfleure	And know that when you use leeches, they help the patient more; and know that sick people do not feel pain from leeches as healthy ones do, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary to apply leeches according to the affected area and severity of the injury. After using leeches, clean the wound with warm water and other treatments until it heals.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When leeches appear in any member and are treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but do not heal, then perform cautery on the affected member according to its size; and if the cauterization is shallow, let it be only a little deep into the flesh. Afterward, treat it with ointments until it heals. Sometimes, cauterization is done on the hand, foot, and back at the nerve endings that cause paralysis in the body, and thus the leech is removed; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	Of bandages
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" occurs and the instruments of medicine are of no use, cauterize it with a shallow cautery according to the size of the sore, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then cure it with wheat flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and goose blood and almond blood, each in equal parts; mix them all together, tie it up with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	cure of scrofula by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When an abscess begins to appear and you wish to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that resembles a circle around the edge of the abscess, some wise men would say to cauterize in the middle of the abscess; however, this does not seem good to me, as I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before; rather, it should be cauterized around with the cautery called "circular", as we have said regarding cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When a person has a disease called "adubelati", which grows slowly or because of the excess it produces, or due to the age of the patient when they are old (meaning very elderly) and have little blood, or due to the time; and you wish to hasten its growth: then cauterize it with small cauteries all around while pricking; afterwards leave it as is. For it will hasten to grow.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely with fire cautery, heat the fire cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the midst of that disease called "adubelati" while the cautery is piercing it all the way, and make the cautery such that the patient feels it moving outside like this: the pathway of the pustule should be even. Afterwards, cure it until it becomes perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	cure with fire using iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but an eating away of the limb, for it consumes limbs like fire dries up dry things. If you see this disease in a place that can be cauterized with fire, then heat the cautery small and large, according to where the disease is; afterwards, cauterize all around until you have destroyed all corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that all corrupted parts are removed. And then leave it for 3 days, and put soft cauterized powder (made from crushed cauterized areas with oil) on the wounds to remove fire burns and all corruption. After the cure by ointments generates flesh. If after 3 days you see no healthy flesh growing, that is good; if not, start cauterizing again in the place where corrupted parts remain. And this eating away is sometimes cured with medicine ague instead of fire cautery, but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for medicine ague in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The growing pains that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often a disease called "clos" affects the feet, which is a large thing swelling and causing pain to the foot. The cauterization of this disease has two methods: fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization. Fire cauterization is when you heat one cautery like a feather from a quill, made of good iron at the size that can pierce the nail all around, and it should have subtle margins; afterwards place it all hot on the nail, and rotate your hand all around the nail until it comes to the root of the nail; and leave it for four days until it starts to emit pus; then make a plaster of malodorous herbs boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on top for the whole night, and remove and will be detached from its roots. Then cure the place with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted by the body internally, and often happens in the hands and feet, then you must provide hot water cauterization; and it is done in this manner: take a copper or iron cane, or a feather from a quill, and place it on the nail and apply a plaster of pains (verrues); and place the cane so that it encompasses all around, then put some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while rotating so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and may find the hot water penetrates deeply to the root; and let the patient endure a little bit of the pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will be detached from all its roots. Do this repeatedly until you have cured all those in the body, then cure them with soothing ointments that soothe skin.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking (trembling)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes due to coldness of the nerves, or fever of four days or other, you should make them 4 or 5 cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and one in the pelvis area, and one on the stomach with the olive-oil cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	of putrid sores (pustules)
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body is filled with pus-filled sores that come from corrupted matter. It is necessary to make a cautery on each head of the sore as soon as it appears, using either a thin needle of myrtle or long root of aristolochia or cauterizing needle. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this way, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter that comes from them is destroyed, and they become healthy; however, it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great displacements of blood from the cut artery at the wound or the abscess incision, or the member's cautery, and similar things; and it is a very bad thing to let it flow out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, if it happens to someone, you should hurry and put your finger on the vein wound, and press as hard as possible to stop the blood flowing out below your finger, and let no more come out; then take olive oil-soaked cauteries of various sizes and apply them until they are all red; then take .i., either large or small depending on the wound and the location in which the artery is cut, and place the cautery on the vein where you have your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a jump occurs when you place your finger on the vein and the cautery is ready, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are near fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Keep doing this one after the other until the blood stops flowing; be careful not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and take care that no other harm comes to the patient; know that when the artery bursts, it cannot be properly stopped when the arteries are large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop the blood; and bind and tighten accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the binding of a tight cloth or places something burning or similar things on it, will not help if it does not work.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no medicine present, you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it remains swollen above the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but wet it with cold frequently so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and remains swollen; and proceed with the inquiry in front of those from whom you need cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases that require fire cautery or burning medicine, their causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; I placed that chapter from the head to the feet, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same way for those who find it easier to understand what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And likewise as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to act foolishly. For many types of people come for treatment. Those who arrive with such illness that they die quickly due to the madness brought about by their disease and the great severity of its malignancy, and from these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of those who give you advice, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; the patient is disrespectful. It is not advisable that you agree with those who come to you who have this manner, but put more consideration in your honor than in your desire, and do not rashly but wisely with regard to what you are certain of, and from which you can profit; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is achieved; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lord grants you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Further, I have organized this chapter by speaking in chapters, following the order of each chapter of cauteries that I have previously described from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand what you need from these.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The full head is filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during childbirth, and sometimes it happens due to reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and all that I have seen quickly dies; therefore it seems to me that I should spend less effort on these treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I have seen one child whose head was filled with water, and it grew larger every day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture gathered underneath the skull bone between the brain and the bone, and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opening from each side, and the pus gushes out when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return: then you must make four incisions within the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture entirely. Afterwards, strain the incisions with cloth and powders, and put vinegar and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; then unbind it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head stretch out gradually, and give the patient dry meat of a moist animal until the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the abscess is at its widest, and join the watery part; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess opens, and the accumulated part of the watery fluid; and do as you can with it; but be careful not to damage the artery; and make sure that some blood flows out, so that the patient dies a natural death from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of boil
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is any disease called "cataract" in the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old and the medicine's cure does not help, then the last cure is the cautery on the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you are going to cover them, the patient must stand with his head back; afterwards, rub the place of the arteries with a rough cloth until they appear, then hold the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the veins open, and the left and right are found behind the ears, and they are tied together; then mark the places to be cut, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts. The incision should reach as far as the bone, and this should be done through the large part of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers together.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open by itself, then you must measure the space of 2 fathoms (about 4 yards), then make an incision to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be released is about 7 cubic inches (cu) and possibly a little more or less according to what the patient can bear. Then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without spurting, then the arrow that was incised does not come out, then hold and bind the wound and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old migraine comes, and the acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and similar things such as an ancient fevered head, and it is treated by methods of medicines but none of them help, then we should cut open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have mentioned.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient bends back the hairs on his temples, and listens for the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and it is not difficult to find unless in some cold people; and if it is found, the patient should grasp its neck with some cloth, then rub the area with a harsh cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the arteries appear clearly; then take the spatumile (a medical instrument) of this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then, gently scrape the skin to expose the artery, then pull it up towards the incisors, and remove carefully all the threads that are under each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it at the tip of the incisor, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two cheeks. Because if it's not cut off, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the .vj. c/, until .iij.; and if the artery is large, you must tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound closes and bleeding comes to a stop; then cut off the excess that is between the two ligatures in the same hour itself, and if you see, you cauterize the wound with the cautery until the bone is cut through; this is the amputation work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are aid for finishing moisters: that is why they are of greater help to the moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place good-made drains on top; and when they are undone, you should cure them with dry medicines that cause inflammation, and with drains until it is healed; if without the cutting of the artery as much as you work, you hurry to close it with a cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze your hand so the blood does not coagulate; and if you do not have this, place your hand on the area until it becomes frozen, and apply cold water frequently and squeeze it as needed; and the harder and slower the artery extraction is, the more it will be easier in the cauterization of this cautery with two edges, but they should be well thickened to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the pulse is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives, one of thick distance, and then when you have pierced through both the thicknesses, and you place the fire hot upon it until it reaches the bone, and cut open the vein in two thicknesses; and they shall be separated between the two heads because it is not always sealed by this cautery from all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes flow out of the veins that are above the testicles of the head and there is no benefit to medical treatment made in this case, and you see the patient writhing with pain, and his forehead seems to tremble like in a fit; and if they are thin and moist so that the hair on the scrotum falls out, and the scrotum is burnt and scorched by the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And it will be called the "contused cure" by the ancients, and you will make it to the patient who has this illness, shave the hair he has on his forehead, then make four cuts or an even cut along the length of the forehead; one of the cuts should be as deep as two fingers from above the eyebrow downwards towards the nose, and the others two at the costal margins above the scrotum, and be careful not to incise the arteries that are at the two costal margins above the scrotum; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound should have the size of three fingers together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and some linen cloth to wipe the blood, then insert the sharp instrument of this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is above the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two cuts completely up to the bone, then proceed from the mid-incision to the other second, and then remove this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the tool called 'cultellaire', which is sharp on one side and soft on the other, not sharp but flexible, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting side towards the cartilage and the soft side against the bone, and push it to reach the mid-incision. And chop all the vessels that descend from the head towards the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where the cartilage opens, and then continue in the mid-incision until the other end; and then equalize the blood flow, and press the level for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each cut, and put damp linen cloth soaked in wine, oil, and rosewater, and ensure that pus does not come in; on the third day untie the stitches, and apply a large amount of cold tetter ointment made with basilicon oil, and other treatments for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh often comes, and you see the hairs thin and small, blurred vision, burned papers; and the hair follicles are itching, and when the head is scratched in pain, and the sick person coughs; then know by these signs that those materials and that catarrh do not come from any other vein, but rather the one which is affected. The cure for this disease is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you command the patient to bend his head backward, then make a large cut across the forehead, and another wide one. In doing so, begin from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood onto a sponge, then apply pressure between the two edges of the cut and put old cotton in there, and bind it with linen thread; then cover it with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful to prevent hot postem; when the bones are removed, you must rub them until char begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote the growth of char.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour, and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster; administer it in these wounds to alleviate pain everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ear is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar things such as iron; seeds, peas, beans; or something flowing like water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear stone or in any other way that does not fit into the ear, nor grows within the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see a stone, distill a little purple oil or camphor oil, then apply extraction; and make him sneeze with medication, and stop his nostrils when sneezing comes, and put pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and hold it above. Often times festering occurs through this cure; and if it does not fester, apply extraction using subtle tweezers as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it bursts through the tweezers, that is good; if not, apply extraction using fine and slender scissors; and if it does not burst through this, make a cane of beeswax and push the head of the cane or opening of the ear strongly, and stop what is around the cane with molten wax so that the fumes cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out forcibly, for often times it bursts forth as we have said; and if it does not burst forth in this manner, take glue from wherever you can find it, put it on any device that is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not burst forth through all the things that we have said, hurry to incise the ear so that abscess comes out and spasms; and the method of incision is that you first anesthetize the patient with opium, then drain the blood according to the strength of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the base of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the incision be as a crescent moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it as far as possible, and suck out hastily to your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is swollen with grain and inflated, administer extraction; and if it cannot be expelled, administer one thin spathule according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make an incision on the grain if you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and absorbent material, as we have said, so that the extraction may be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In water, therefore, the patient must use a warm wash with first-degree condiments and fill the ear with soft cotton. He should lie on that ear itself or where the water falls. If it jumps out because of this, that is good. But if it does not, take many thin and light pieces of stone according to the length of your finger, heat one slightly in fire; and make the patient hold one end of a piece in his ear, and press with another stone from the other side, and strike another stone on the one in the ear; and do not cease to strike stone against stone until the water comes out completely, and it jumps out completely; and if you see, take a stalk, and put one end of the stalk in the ear, and the other end hold near fire until the most burned stalk is burned; then repeat this with other straws until the water comes out completely, as we have said in the previous section.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals such as mice and similar things, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large and can be felt, introduce extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs, when you treat it as we have said in the previous section or using distillations which do not help, if there are no worms visible, take fine tweezers and grasp them at this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. Push the most subtle head into the ear according to the degree of the patient's suffering, then firmly grasp the entire shape; do this often until all the worms come out. If they do not obey to come out, plug the shape with cotton as I have said in the previous section; and if they do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the removal of earwigs, and you will find them where you treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is to be made of silver or lead which is inserted into small openings, and on top with a distilling dish; and for pressing inside the distillation, use one instrument of lead well made for this purpose. And if you see a plug and wrap it around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see fit in the pipe, and let the pipe be in the ear. Then push the plug into the cotton and press gently until the oil distills or becomes hot in the ear. Let the patient smell inside, and the distillation should be heated with fire so it is as it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be good if it is too cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage (clogging) of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having some opening in the ears; and this same thing happens with adults due to ear injury or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes occurs deep within the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there is a small hole in the ear, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes out completely and cannot be seen, it is serious healing in many positions, and in such a case, you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening clearly apparent, then open it with this spatula of the form specified here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And sharp and cutting in front and behind entirely, so as not to burn the ear; if the opening is of cartilage or skin of the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers, and gently remove it all.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opening is deep in the ear, take a sharp, subtle scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the side of the ear. If you feel the opening that causes pain to the patient's hearing, pierce it gently, but be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals: take a cloth and soak it in strong rosewater, and powder vitriol over it (broken); if you see the ear swelling, then pull out the cloth and apply another cloth soaked in salve made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If discharge of blood comes out, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the blood discharge which are called distillations.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal (carbon)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that come in paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and strike it with a spatula from its roots; then put on the place vitriol ground.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	If not removed by other means, then cauterize the lenticular cautery gently and slowly, and cauterize after the incision is beneficial; and many times they heal again, for nothing stays from their roots; and when cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and will not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Often come in paper the eyes appear like hailstones in shape and hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "grandine", which is a gathering of large moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take care that the grandine remains silent from one side and the other, and it is an easy thing to know; then open it widely, then lightly peel off each part, then seize it with the forceps and squeeze. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, then do not bother the patient; and if the tear is large, bind it up with a stitch, and care for it until it heals; but if it is small, do not exert force because the onions will restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and take hold of the grandine with forceps, squeeze and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, then do not cause pain; when the grandine is squeezed, apply salted oil to the wound and care for the affected area until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is embedded in fabrics made of paper, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it greatly hurts their eyes, and they come down with catarrh at dawn, and cannot endure the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces immediately, sleep on top, and their fabrics are damp under their eyelids that the exinach has covered in oil. And when you press the area between your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.
