And the method of work is that the patient places their head on a clean surface; then take one linen cloth and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, and place it above; then press between your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the middle with a sharp spatula, and not larger than the wound made in vein suture; and cut through the skin as far as you see the exinach; and in various positions, exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then hold the piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to the left and right until it is dispersed; and be careful not to widen the incision or reach the oil with the spatula, do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, lift up the wound slightly; then pull it apart as we have said, wet some bandages with oil and water, place them on the wound, and hold it in place with bindles.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for those who grind seeds and place them on top to corrupt the moisture that is present, then heal it until it is healthy. If an abscess heats up at the site, treat it with plasters soothing it until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural and they are nurtured, they harm the eyes and bring about types of diseases such as constant tearing and softening of the paper-like growths, which causes destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure them: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine for ague according to what was mentioned in the previous chapter on cauterization, or by incision and suturing, or by caustics, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your healthy side, then turn the paper-like growth from the eye towards your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, push an awl with one filament through it; and remove the margin of the paper or the hair that grows from those hairs, taking one filament across the entire paper, and shave it off; then make a shallow groove in the part beneath the paper, below the hairs, covering the entire spatula blade from the large tear to the small; then pull out one filament, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen under the paper, then mark on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the seed of mirte, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the size that you see raising the paper which has been previously determined.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if the amount of paper that needs to be removed is large due to the softening of the paper, then make a groove on both lines that you marked and start from the large tear until it is small; one of the cuts should be near the natural hairs, and push the incisor into one of the two corners of the cut, then peel everything; then bring the two lips together with a suture using an awl with a single thread of fine linen, squeeze out the blood, and make the excess filaments sticky with something gluey, if you want to do this; and if not, leave the sutures and the filaments for 2-4 days without treatment, then treat the wound without suture using drying and constricting agents, since the paper heals at the edge of the wound and the sutures are loosened (as the ancients say), but this is a task done with fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And in another way: and it is that you make the paper of a figure which should be as the fern leaf of myrtle, as we have mentioned, in three openings according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then make that which surmounts the small points equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are not able to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and stick it into the figure; and put another thread through the large opening, and the second thread through the small, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then move your hand evenly, and draw all the skin which you have marked, as we have mentioned, then sew together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and let it heal until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of paper turns into something: you must use what we have said about incising, but stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of cancers is as follows: you should convert the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two cages by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and width as broad as the spatula is; and bind the two pieces together where the threads are; then assemble the one and the other carefully on top of the paper with oil, and bind the two cages from the two parts; leave it for some days, and the skin that has been bound will die, rot, and fall off, leaving a hole.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time or if you need to force it, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, remove the paper and the hairs will not grow anymore; this is the shape of the two cages that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The first sentence to translate:
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the channel (tunnel) is treated and the hairs do not come out, then draw the channel down to the length of the thread you have arranged, until the channel comes out from the opening above and you see it through the oil; then draw out the channel and the thread, close the eye and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and grows new skin over it; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair and let it grow with it, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the abscess (boil) of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or porriture comes in the oil, it happens in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. It occurs suddenly through a wound, or from cutting, or by fire, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The method of treatment is that you cut the joint and separate the lips, put threads of flax inside, and let it stay until it heals; it must not be treated with things that dry out or restrict it. For if you do so, the disease becomes worse than the first time; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the broth of water or vinegar and flax seeds boiled, and immediately apply the melted beeswax in any oil, wrap it in a linen cloth, and treat it with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the remedy for your cure is to ensure that it does not heal in the same way as before; and this work that we have said is not effective unless proper attention is paid to this disease, so that it does not return in its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fat that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cauterization and things similar; and the method of operation in it is that you take a needle, in which there are two double threads, and pierce through the fat, starting from the left eyelid to the right, so that the threads come out in two heads of the fat; then lift the fat over the whole needle, and hold with one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should be, that is good; if not, take one razor and put it in the cut, turn the paper, and make two cuts on the side where the paper thickens inside, and let the heads of the cuts be at the corners of the incision that you made, and let a corner be formed so that when they are assembled, the shape is as the shape of a letter that has the name "Greek J"; then remove that fat according to the width that its sides are sharp below the paper, then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then treat it with the medicine that we have said for softening and healing until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the sickness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make a deep incision under the hairs of the paper, as described earlier; then you should draw out between the two layers of the skin like I said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare devices with all their might to return the figure to its natural form; and the sick themselves, according to what work and instruments are required in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the hairs of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sewing occurs in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural work, then you must insert the tip of a razor blade under the paper, lift it up; and stretch it using pliers until you reach the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too pointed, so that the sick man does not suffer from the too-sharp spatula causing damage to the oil; and your incision, from which you peel off the assembled area, should be gentle, allowing the paper to return to its natural form; and heal all of the assembled area, making it sometimes in oil of vinegar unsalted and sweet leaven, then put a tent made of linen between the paper and oil, and place wool dampened with egg on top of the oil; and after three days use warm water and healing salves until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail has two kinds: it is either nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, or it's not nerve-like but resembles white congealed moisture that, when touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, cannot be removed; and both begin at the great cuticle and grow little by little until they cover the whole nail and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take a piece of paper with your hand, then take the nail with tweezers of small double curvature and hold it above; then take a needle and put one horse hair or ox hair and a strong thread on it; bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce through the nail, and pass the whole needle through it, tie the nail with a thread and hold it above, and peel off all the skin from the side of the nail that was close to the cuticle and the silk until the hair reaches the head, then chop off the remaining in the root of the cuticle with every subtle spatula and small force, and leave the natural skin or cuticle so that no blood comes out of the cuticles as usual; and sometimes the nail is incised only on the edge and at the tip, as we have said; then peel off all the spatumile from it in this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatula does not touch the skin layer and break it, and that the prunelle is not pierced; and after incision pour oil a small amount of boiled egg yolk and let it rest with a litargire collar, leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicines; and they grow as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, then open the oil of the patient, take the spatula gently and slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Lift the nail gently and if you see that it does not shrink and the reason is pressing on it, then distill from your mouth collyrium made of litargyre and red collyrium and boiled egg yolk into the oil and stopper it until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing contradicts you in oil (i.e., if it is an abscess), then let it discharge, and first heal the abscess with hot water until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the arm is harmful in oil (meaning an abscess) by great damage, then suspend it at the joint and cut off a part but not too much, so that tears do not come; then distill red colloidal oil made of litargyre (an antimony compound).
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which arises on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The first hairs of some men sometimes grow red, cover the nail and are raised above the papery skin and resemble a rosebud; and this condition is such that the patient places his head on the healthy part, then he opens the eyes, and all of the red hair that corresponds to the nail should be removed in this way, and it should be held firm with force; then cut the first red hair, and continue cutting all the way to the root until the end, but ensure that you do not wound the skin during the operation; and make the incision with a spatula as we have said in the nail incision and the small forces of which one extracts the skin, as shown by the form after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	When the incision is completed and all the hair is removed, apply oil of linseed or you distill red colloid and similar corrosive medicines on it with a flax cloth soaked in egg white to ensure proper healing; if something remains and the wound becomes cold, and you doubt that it is properly healing, leave the oil and treat the wound with calming remedies for cold wounds; then return to your work when it is healed, and thus do this for each hair that is soaked in the oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must lighten the cure of each oil with natural methods; and in case of accidental injury, in work involving iron; and never insert your hand into any of these operations unless you see that the limb is strong enough to endure that operation.
des voines des eulz	The veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The red veins that are covered over the oil and take over its function and weaken the eye entirely for all days. Therefore, first it is necessary to examine if the eye, in which the vein is located, has any other disease except the vein; then cool it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your healthy hand, then press those veins all along for the entire length as wisely as possible, and let the hands be subtle double as follows:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two lengths of the cloth folded twice by degree, as follows:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then collect the veins subtly with force, and squeeze out the blood hour after hour, until you see the veins move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that only these veins are affected; and when you have done this, if it distills into green and red coloured oil for correcting what is left behind in the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and sure of abscessing coldly, then resume according to this manner as long as it is healthy; and this is the form of force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is a cavity in it where it should die, and you must cut open the abscess along that area, removing all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, then use all the equipment that is shown here; it is called "rough head", and should be made of iron and shaped like this (referring to a certain shape as presented in the drawing):
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone that is corrupted, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is crushed; do this repeatedly, then restore the position of the medicine extractors.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is fused, and char (possibly pus) arises, and the body of the bone is also fused and remains in that state for 40 days, without healing or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs - it is known to be healthy; if not, there is no other remedy except to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one iron rod according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft be attenuated until the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the rod on the bone of the nose and move your hand an inch away from it, then turn the iron rod completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through his nose if he keeps his hand on his nostril; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the pus arises and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the nose; it is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the nasal passage
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance to the ship [the body], and it does not decrease, you must hold the patient; then clean [the eyes], then apply plasters or ointment without causing pain, then apply oil - a liniment made from aloe, acacia, incense, and saracocolla - and hold [the eye], and apply the plaster on bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the amount required by the eyes; then hold it together with a tough bandage and repeat the application of plasters without causing pain; then remove the plasters and leave the oil held for day and night, and if the liniment becomes soft, you must hold it firmly; then remove the liniment after day and night, and if you see the eyes heal, that is good; if not, repeat the application of the plaster and the liniment and the bandages until the eyes are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The bursting of a swollen cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the uvea (the middle layer of the eye), followed by an opening and forced expulsion of paper-like substances resembling grain of resin and appearing alarming; then if you see it covered, the treatment is such that you insert a needle into the root of the affected area up to where it is above, then insert another needle with double thread from the edge of the wound; and make it pierce through, leaving the first needle according to its position; then hold the eye's lid tightly and tie a part of the uvea around it, applying pressure; then remove the needle and apply oiled linen cloth abundantly over the area; and leave it until the threads stick with the uvea, then cure the affected area with soothing substances until the wound heals; and at times, the wound is restrained by the uvea on each side of a circular bandage of fabric, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes seem large in appearance, perforate them with a thin spatula filled with oil, remove the albuginea (the middle layer of the eye) and drain the fluid from the eyes; then let it heal completely.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the beak of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not foreign, but rather it is an abscess formed in the oil (oil sac), appearing like an inflammation draining pus, yet it is not a real inflammation; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a seat prepared and straight. Then take the head between your hands from two sides, and move it until you see the abscess rise to your eyes; then it should be lanced, and the pus should not drain and the light should disperse. Let the patient observe things as he usually does; if it does not drain under, know that it is an inflammation, and if the draining of the abscess is not prepared as we have said. Seat the patient between your hands, then take a fine spatula and poke through the cornified membrane and the corona repeatedly, until the abscess comes out. When it is issued, let it distill in hot, sweet oil mixed with honey, or hot oil or fenugreek boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	oil abscesses
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similarities with abscesses in the division, and what is necessary to puncture; if you do according to health. It is required that you seat the patient between your hands crossed, away from the light for the sun, and hold the oil tightly and very firmly; then place a piece of paper of the oil on your left hand if the hairs are on the left side or on your right hand if they are on the right side; then take with your right hand, if the hairs are on the left side, the instrument called "almagda", or take it with your left hand if they are on the right side; then place the point of the instrument near the corona by the thickness of a fingernail in the whiteness of the oil at the lower eyelid; then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and apply pressure to your hand until it pierces through the whiteness of the oil, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the length of the pathway almagda should be at the full measurement of the space from the eyelash to the end of the blackness; and this is the corona of the oil; if you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the cornified membrane, then place the instrument until it reaches the bottom or the abscess; then press it down a pathway after another. If the abscess bursts now, let the patient observe before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the second vein rises again, put force with the instrument, and when it is pierced and does not rise, gently pull it back slightly by rotating your hand slowly; then put a little gemstone oil inside. Then place linen soaked in oil of roses and abundant egg over it, and seal it with oil. We, and those from our time, place common powder with plenty of egg on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the gemstone oil cannot enter due to hardness, because some men have very hard eyes, then you must take the tool called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore perforate only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make it gently shallow, then put gemstone oil as we have said; and when the work is completed, prepare the patient to sleep for seven hours in a dark room on his back; be careful of all movements, take light foods, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in the same dark room, examine his vision, let him see certain things, and then rebind him for seven more days; it is not necessary that you perform this, during the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you relieve it because the eyes rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess swells up, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes an abscess; and when it is soothed, you should then lance the wound and place a linen cloth over it to cover for any day, and remain in that dark room. Then gradually leave the room and convert to your quarters; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iram, who told us that in their country everyone has a large pear-shaped swelling, so that fluid accumulates, but I have never seen anyone with such a thing in our land, nor have I read of it in the books of ancient people; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of almagda shapes, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of linen properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these (should) be in the same subtlety, and the rear ones in four corners.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes the nose produces various sores that appear similar to scorpions at their feet; and if there are any that have a sore swollen with green color, or a soft sore of white color. In that case, for the soft sore that is not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun, open his nostrils, and put onion juice on those sores, then pull them out; afterwards, hold what you can with the thin sharp spatula until you know that the sore is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be covered, you shall open it all, i.e., with subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if there is no pus, or an abscess covered, help it as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is drained and all the charred matter is removed, then pour in oil, vinegar, or hot water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If there is no opening and moisture reaches the palace (palate), know that it is healthy; if moisture does not perforate as needed, know that char has grown in the bone above, so instruments do not come to cut; then put a thick thread of flax, which is boiled and moistened with our hands, between each stitch of about one finger's breadth; and insert the floss into the patient's nose as far as possible, and pull it out while smelling until pus comes out from the nose; and many times do this as children in school do, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to perform it; then hold the head that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other while we who are the floss-pullers are there. Do this until you know that the floss has corrupted the char; then remove the floss, squeeze the pus, and moisten the flax in Egyptian ointment, and return it to the nose as before; do this for 4 days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that remains of the char; and then put a plank drain in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as oil and medicines are distilled through.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with a closed neck, and you shall lead it so; and if you see, make a closed tube, and the instruments should be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often in the head of the nose there arises a sickness called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning, and burn it completely with cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed too long while it is still small, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an aggravated abscess, for when one touches it in any way, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of a dark color, and you can cover it completely, let the patient empty it and cut it cautiously without fear, and cure the place with dry things that absorb.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilage joints, it benefits little, unless in some men. Therefore, when this occurs to anyone, you should examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then you align the two lips to a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scour all parts of their joint as they heal, then align the two lips to a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder and incense crushed; and put some plaster of strong or other plaster adhering on top of the powders, and let it remain until it dries, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in the belly stitch; or with thread, as we mentioned earlier.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For men, within the lips there occurs an abscess hard, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut open each one, take it with tweezers and crush it in every part; afterwards apply the vitriol powder to the wound until the blood is stopped; then apply alum to heal the wound until it heals completely.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often arises on the gums a swelling called "albulus"; you should hold it with tweezers and crush it at its root, allowing the pus to flow out; then apply powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders to the area; if the swelling returns after cutting, which often happens, you should crush it again and cauterize it; it does not return after cauterization; these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	The sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, sores are assembled in the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs that are unsightly; and sometimes the tooth becomes black and yellow and hollow as corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scabs that appear, until nothing remains; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and for the yellowish and other blemishes, until they are cleaned; and if you remove that which is at the root first, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have everything removed; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments to scrape them, according to what the work requires, because the scraper used to clean the teeth has other shapes than the one used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a tooth for pain, you must delay extraction as much as possible, because it should not be done at all; for it is a very high substance up until the point that there is no excuse to shave.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is forced to draw the tooth, it is necessary that you are certain of the bad tooth. Many times, pain deceived the patient, and they believe it is a healthy tooth, and pull the good one; yet, the pain does not depart until the bad one is removed, as we have seen in the past; and when you are absolutely certain of the bad tooth, you must cut around the tooth at every side with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it gently with your fingers or fine pliers at the first edge and little by little until it is completely loosened; then firmly close the pliers; and hold the patient's chin in your saint between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Then draw the tooth straight out, and if it does not break off, take one of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, as you have done before. And if the teeth are perforated and eaten away, it is necessary to fill it with cloth where the holes are; then hold it subtly with pliers so that it does not break when pulling; and very carefully work around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part behind, and the patient will have greater pain from the root later due to malice. Also, beware of doing as ignorant men do, who sometimes break the chariot due to their hastiness and recklessness; and they do not bring what we have mentioned; but sometimes they bring about great illness due to the roots that remain, or because they break the chariot, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or oil and soap; and if bleeding persists, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which quiet the tooth roots first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and toothed to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains after pulling, then you must put cotton moistened in butter on it for 1 or 2 days until the butter is absorbed, then insert the pliers called "algefri", so that the tooth looks like a beak of a bird; and they should be made inside as a chisel and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tools, you must peel back the skin all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as a pincer, of which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Be large and thick so as not to break it, and if the root jumps out through these tools, that is good; otherwise, use all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one assists with this instrument having two prongs, of which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool which appears to be large pliers, in its form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not break, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other tools which are not counted; and the wise masters discover their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease shows, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach any tool due to diversity in each case; and if it breaks the cart or another bone where it should be, then look for the tools that are required, which I told you, and help with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, but not slip away, but be able to hold and remove it; then restore the place of medicines suitable for that, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, use all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape, and the form is ugly, even in women virgins, you must know if the tooth is not born after the dent, and it is not in the correct place, and cannot be corrected or smoothed: then file [the tooth]; and if it is exposed with the tooth, take this instrument, as shown by the form below, resembling a small beak, made of sharp iron at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the file is held in hands for long hours due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be smoothed, file it with a flat file as shown below:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used for making needles; and file the tooth little by little with the file in hands gently, so it does not move too much while chewing; then plane the end entirely with any file, and if the root is too sharp and it bites the tongue, you must smooth the sharpness until it is even, so it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When teeth fall out, either by impact or falling, and the patient cannot press up on it when eating unless it falls, you treat them with medicines that restrict, but this is not effective; instead, they should be restrained with a gold wire, as silver wires turn green and decay, but gold does not change ever; whether the wire is medium or thick or thin depends on the space between the teeth; if you see the teeth are moving, take the wire and put it double between two healthy teeth, then place the chips between the loose teeth, whether there are one or more, until you reach the sound tooth from the other side; then start covering again up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and skillfully, so it does not move; and your grip at the root of the tooth should be firm so that it cannot escape. Then grab the chips with tweezers, assemble them, place them back between the sound tooth, ensuring it doesn't touch the tongue; then leave it tight for as long as possible until it heals, if they disconnect or the wires break, re-tighten it with another wire; if it remains and serves for the entire time, that is the form of teeth and the shape of the alignment of two healthy teeth, and two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place, as we have said; and let no one who is not skilled and patient interfere with it; and sometimes the shape of a bone tooth from an animal is made and placed at the place where it lacks, and it should be held and served for a long time as described earlier.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	There are times when this wound comes under the tongue either naturally or through an injury of a healed wound; and the treatments for it are as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head still, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous wound with a large bandage until the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or pain, and it is a sudden injury from a wound, insert an arrowhead and cover that dislocation with a large bandage; but make sure the cut is not too deep, because there is an artery underneath; and when you have done this, raise the rose-colored and ashen, or cold, level of the wound and put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind it to the patient every night so that the level does not heal. And if discharge of blood comes out, apply vitriol powder; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another remedy until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of dark or black color or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards blistering, and there is moisture, throw in an arrowhead, and make a small incision on both sides with a thin spatula, and free it from one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, apply vitriol powder until it is drained completely; then raise the rose-colored and ashen level, and cure it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	The abscess of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes inside the throat come swellings called "godath," which are properly called the two almonds. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but let it remain until it is ripe, and then you will cut it open, or it will burst by itself; and if it is of white color returning, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check if the abscess is cooled down and calmed. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your hand, and open his mouth and take the serjeant between his hands, and press the tongue under the entire instrument, so that this is its shape; and it should be made of silver or thin brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue under the entire instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the awl and poke it into the almond, and pull it upwards as much as you can; pull any fabric away from there, then cover it with the instrument, so that this is its shape, like a vise; and although the head may be bent, one end to another, and they are very sharp, made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the coppersmith's pliers, of which form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the coppersmith's pliers, of which form is as follows: grasp one of the almonds and squeeze the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot, sharp, and astringent substance, and if bleeding occurs, gargarize the patient with hot, or scorches of green grapes cooked, or twigs of myrtle, and similar things until the wound is cauterized; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses than the two almonds may appear in the throat, if they appear, squeeze them in the same way as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside the throat, to wit, an abscess of small size; and I had cautiously closed the whole throat, such that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passageway, nor eat or drink, and she would have died within one to two days if she continued like this.
