The abscess was so large that it had filled two fingers by the two passages of the throat. I therefore punctured it at once, and pulled out a bone, followed by a large piece of pus; then I sealed the other passage in the throat, opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after which, I punctured the abscess again, cut off a part of it, and not much blood came out; and thus the blocked passageway in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink hot water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away from that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew again, filling up the space that I had seen, becoming very large; at that point, I tricked it and cauterized it inside the throat: in this way, the abscess stopped growing; and I left those places, and let God do with them as He wished after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye swells and becomes long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the swollen abscesses are alleviated, and it becomes subtle, it is necessary to cut; and if it is round and swollen but not long; and it is blood-colored or of dark or black color, it is necessary to make an incision. For there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, depending on its size and length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned above; then poke the onion into the eye, drag it out, and cut it at .i. of .ij. stitches that I have said in the incision of .ij. almonds. And it is necessary not to cut beyond the natural limit; for if you do so, it hurts the voice, and speech. After the incision, use what we have said in the incision of .ij. almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient fears the cutting, it is necessary to use an instrument for cauterization to allay fear. And the manner of cautery is sharp heat. And it is that the patients put their head in your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned or chapter of cautery, and hold with hot live coals, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and employ the handle of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a comb or hand put the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine without going down to the throat, and the blood. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, the amount of half an hour, until you see it swell and the bites of the medicine are alleviated; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument to the entire cotton into the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for 4 or 5 days. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, restart it, and after the cautery suck out around the eye, with a cotton swab in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and wash it with cold water, and treat it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not just cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile and yarrow and origanum and rue and wormwood and similar herbs, put them all together or any of these in one pot, and place it on the fire; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one instrument with hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it [the instrument] should be made of silver or lead, and one end pushed into the patient's mouth until the steam rises to the eye through the tube while the eye is being mortified; afterwards repeat often, until the eye dries, and ensure that you do not do this at the beginning of an abscess boil, for many things can happen; and do not use this unless in the presence of a declining abscess boil. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put a chicken feather inside the head of the patient so that his mouth does not get too hot; as the chicken feather will not burden the mouth with steam, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it [the abscess] adheres to the throat with bone or splinter of fish, or something else; therefore, you must pull what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in it; and if that does not open up and returns to the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of seaweed, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, if it adheres, you must pull on the thread; and if it does not come out as we have said, take one stick according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and raise the head high; and watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, as both will come to harm, nor push the bone in; instead, it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because he may be moved or the thing is loose; if he pushes down, or draws it back completely, keep pushing equally until it has gone.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the saliva is medicinal, as I have said in the division, by means of medicine's cure; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, since you press his tongue against the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the saliva, take a small pair of scissors or subtle tweezers, which are suitable for this purpose. If this is not effective, take a hair-rope and insert it into the patient's throat, then push down the end of the rope with a hot iron and repeat this often. Dip the patient in cold water all day. Then take a full ounce of cold water, open the mouth, pour it inside without swallowing, and move it around with your hand frequently; and as soon as the saliva feels the water, it falls out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then you should suffumigate the patient with asefetide, at the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will not subside easily. The method of suffumigation is that you take one pot or one that has charcoal within, and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and put the head of the instrument into it; then pour your suffumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes to the nostrils; and the nose will now be affected, and if it does not subside, then continue the suffumigation many times; allow the patient to thirst, and eat salty and alkaline things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out under this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument to treat the nose, is like corbeled tweezers for entering the throat; and resembling the beak of a syringe, and having asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot lose; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	"Many resemble abscesses, as recalled in this chapter from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and these are in .ij. ways, of which the first is like itself, and due to moisture. The second way is for the joints that are in the body. For abscesses on the head are different than those from the foundation, and abscesses from the charnut joint are different than those that come at jointures, and each should be judged in its work."
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	"And if there are abscesses that one should not perforate until the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if there are those that need to be perforated when they have become hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses near jointures. For when an abscess comes near a jointure, and it is left until it is surrounded, by chance the ligament and nerve of the jointure may become corrupt, causing contraction in that member. Or the abscess is from the main part of the body, and if you delay the perforation until it has ripened, it will harm the main part; or it is from the foundation, and if it is perforated before it has ripened, it should not be perforated without digestion being completed, except for that which is from the foundation, that it may burst completely, and be drained internally, and a fistula comes; and it cannot heal in a long time."
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the disappearance of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and reduction in size of the abscess head, and other signs; and you should make a small incision in the perforation area that depends on the location of the abscess, and where it has opened; and the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in all even places where there is no pus."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	1. In those who plunge (sink/fall), according to that member. And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce before this point, it will cause the body to bleed excessively and fill with much pus; and possibly swell and deepen the wound. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no head (opening) in the abscess, like a superficial one, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only some part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing out incorrectly; do this many times gradually, until the pus is all out. However, if the patient is weak, or a woman giving birth, or small children, or old and decrepit people, the pus may jump out occasionally with the release of the pus, possibly causing the death of the patient, and you will not be at fault. Therefore, proceed with great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and examine if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a flat area, bring linen or old cotton threads; and if it is large abscesses and there is much pus, it is necessary that you stuff a thread in each one so they come against each other; and if you have cut part of the skin in the abscess and shaved around it, fill it with old cotton or flax rags without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and alcohol, and moisten one cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.  If the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book to the affected areas; and if it is winter, or the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, you must place hot wet towels on them; and if it is summer, and the limbs are fleshy, you must place wet towels on them, or cold water and oil, or cold wine and oil for three days as we have said; then drain the abscess, lance it and treat it until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: here I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and now comes the chapter.
des soros	on les faut oster et conforter par l'aiguille et les poudres
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come in the head, there are methods known to us that are in linens, like the knot of a vine, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty with moisture, like boils; and some are hard and rough at the base, without any doubt that arteries do not oppose them. And the procedures for the neck, it is to be experienced with every tool used which is called "entromissoire", from which this form follows, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, they do it above the long one. And when the moisture is evacuated, they scrape without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when nothing is left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; otherwise, in water and linen, and apply it to the wound and leave it until the next day; and those who have been delayed at night will heal. And the following day, repeat the cotton, as before, for three days, until you know that it does not stay at night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess is one nut size, squeeze it according to this form, longwise; and throw your fingers around it, and scrape from all sides, and apply your entire care to draw pus out of the place where it lies; and if arteries oppose you, do as I told you before. And do the same for the abscess if it is hard, and treat and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the hard abscess and the moist one is lighter, because they have little blood. And if any of these abscesses or head has no moisture, and among them was one abscess that I squeezed or head of an old woman; and found the abscess like a hard nut, rough and white, and could not break; and if iron had been applied to it, it would have made an equal wound as from a hard nut. In other abscesses coming from the head, whether they are those that come at the heads of children and the roots of the ears, they should be opened every day for the longest time depending on the case, in order for the pus to escape; and they are cured as needed.
des scrophules	of the scrofula (scrofulas)
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times this abscess occurs at the neck, under the ears, and in the groin, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and they are connected with one another. And each scrofula is properly within its cavity, as the aposteme of the head and the shoulder, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malicious ones that do not wish to obey health. Therefore, when you see it in good condition to touch, and it appears like the color of the body, mute on all sides and not swollen near the neck or artery or conduit, and not inflamed; if you have need to lance it, cut it open from above, and remove the scab from each part, and set the two lips of the curette as the oneches, if necessary, as we have said in apostemes of the head; and draw it out gently and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula too much or cut deeply, so that your hand does not slip, and look carefully so as not to cut what should not be.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to finish your work, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; leave it until the abscess is calmed down and the wound softens and begins to purify. And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work as long as you complete it; then ask your guide if there remain any small scrofulas, cut and clean them. If there is a large one at the root of the scrofula, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it hang, without harm; then use old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on the wound and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them up immediately since there will be no excess due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and draw pus out, and sew as we have said before. Those scrofulas with superfluidity, pierce where it has grown closed; and pierce as described above, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply a charmed ointment until it heals.
de squinance	And if you excise the entire squinchy bump (a term used to describe a lump or swelling in medieval medicine), it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them up immediately since there will be no excess due to the size of the squinchy bump. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and draw pus out, and sew as we have said before. Those squinchy bumps with superfluidity (excessive fluid), pierce where it has grown closed; and pierce as described above, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply a charmed ointment until it heals.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shape of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinch (a condition), the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" should be opened; and no help should be given by those with abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2 tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it should be covered to prevent the danger of choking caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it should be cut below four circles or two small cuts through the center, between the four circles or by the size of the scythe, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the neck is swollen at the incision of the epiglottis, there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long behind.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then you must stretch out the skin of the throat all along, then cut open the neck until it reaches the trachea; and cut off the vessels carrying blood, if you see anything, and then tie the sutures as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the incision of the trachea which bursts through the broken neck, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, bring the two lips of the wound together gently, and close it completely with a splint; then administer medicines that promote healing, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi said not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead and the breath has left him/her.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then, squeeze the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he/she breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it has passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they instructed to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife, and stab it in her throat, and cut off part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was summoned to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and knew that it had not opened up or been directed anywhere other than the throat, and the wind was going through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly sewed up the wound and healed it until it was healed.  */*   And when I had finished healing it, I realized that she had died before my arrival.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And there is no damage to the lady except that her voice was hoarse, and she returned to her condition afterwards.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the case of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess colored like a pigeon's egg and occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	The accidental is also according to two ways: one resembling fatty tissue and the other resembling an abscess that comes from us by way of arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear and one should not do anything forceful except in the small one, and it must be proven and searched thoroughly with all the introduction.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as a small abscess and it does not open anywhere, if you press on it, do so like with fat, and pull off the entire head, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And carefully examine [it] thoroughly, and heal it as necessary, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods of ours are there, which I will describe all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is necessary that I tell you the whole difference which is between cause and effect.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue (discharge) is heat and fever lasting, until the eruptions have passed, and the purification has been completed; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without doubt there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains one pustule (abscess), which is its own sac and is similar to the color of the body, and starts like a blister and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two types, either fat or moist, and have much the same color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of the sick, that you test and inquire first about all the equipment which is called "entromissoire", according to its form or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiry for abscesses by us is that you take or the most moist place that you find within the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the instrument, and be careful that it does not fall.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out from the wound, make it so that it becomes colored as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no moisture comes out after the incision, know that it is fat, then make a cross-shaped incision, take hold of it with forceps, and gently peel off from both sides and watch the coat that it comes out healthy with the lancet;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you cannot draw it out healthy, draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there is nothing left, it returns many times again.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there remains a little bit and it does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, hold the wound closed, place warm things over the abscess to relieve the pain, and treat with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If the wound is large, make two lips of the wound, and treat with what cures sores.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein bursts against you or another, hurry and use vitriol powder, let it lie for two or four days, until the wound scabs over, and let the pus of blood settle; then cover what remains of the wound with a poultice.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here is the translation of the provided Old French text:
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also similar to needles used for sewing sacks, and they are of citron cane, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow have more value, and they are more sharpened with black wood for encircling the boils of a fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and come in three types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of ulcers are much alike, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and some ulcers have two hump-shaped appearances in four ways;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and some ulcers have four humps in four ways, and some ulcers have two humps and others only one hump, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these (things) that are sharp is pointed, and those who do not cut completely from one side, from which we scrape the nerves, so as not to strike the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And from these openings are the incisions replied in stitches, so that the patient does not hurt himself at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	They are of three kinds: large, small, and medium-sized, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And it should not be used anywhere else but in soft flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes another small instrument like scorches of pliers, shaped in this form, is used to draw blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at the location that bleeds to stop the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes again according to this large form:   (This translation assumes that "copement des voines" refers to stopping the bleeding of the veins, which might not be accurate without more context.)
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to become corrupt, until they seem like female breasts:
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them, it is necessary to be according to this form of the following line: b to g:   (This translation assumes that "b" refers to a certain point on a scale and "g" refers to another point on a different scale, but without more context, it's hard to be sure.)
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then, scrape the fat, apply medicine on the wound made of inciting char, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it heals.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the limb bends downwards, it is swollen due to its size as happens with women, they make two incisions on top of it, through two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	by which one is held to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scorch the skin that is between the two lips [of the wound], and remove the fat, and bring what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest or due to blood flow, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it digests the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses from the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses coming from the buttocks are types of scrofulas (hard) or they may contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form: from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowel in the abscess is emptied, you should use old cotton for the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and heal it with an ointment until it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (or scrofulous lesions), then make incisions in it as we have said before for scrofula, and if the wound becomes swollen, bring fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The cutting of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin over it heals, there are often abscesses, and the same thing happens at an opened vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows it thus as for the artery, then the abscesses are long in depth;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your fingers, then it feels narrow; and when it is for the vein, then the wound appears wide open;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is under the nails and angles, and near the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the iron cure must be avoided, and the one at the neck should also be avoided, and in the case of swelling from the artery, make an incision through the skin along the length;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then make the incision in the bellybutton, and carefully separate the artery from the intestines, while it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle and make it pass through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two inches, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then pierce the space between the two ligaments with a probe until it passes through, and break open the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a poultice made of yarrow root, while the ligament heals.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this with ointment until it heals.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to the vein being opened, then you must smear your hand with what you can get from the abscess all over the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then push the needle under the place that you hold with your hand, and make it pierce through, and have it double thread so that you can pull it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I told you, or bind it with one of two parts to each of the two sides with thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will pass through, push another needle through all the way under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then compress the abscess until the excess comes out, then compress the exudate from the wound and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then treat it with plasters and liniments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in arteries and veins, they come in nerves when injured or from excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	This happens more often in the shoulders and thumbs and all joints where there are connections, that is, severe abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it causes pain in various positions.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strained forcefully, the patient feels pain, but it is not all over the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it should be completely immobilized from all sides, neither forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and one who is in the joints should not be covered by iron; by chance it may cause contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is on the forehead or the head, should use the cupping glass.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, grasp it with forceps and strike at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, lift it up at the edge, peel it off, then pierce and sew the wound together and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Large lumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there occurs in bellies and nowhere else but this is a disease called "fungus", resembling worms, with subtle roots and large heads; there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	I saw one man who had two bellies that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference between them; they were white, had a thin root, were split open, and continued to leak moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found one weighing 16 ounces and the other 5 pounds. The abdominal cavity in the incision appears moist if the patient is wet, and the color of the growth is pale and moist with a thin root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the neck is swollen with pus, and the fire cautery is in your presence. For in cutting it often comes too great discharges of blood, and if the blood escapes without you being there, hurry up to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron cut, take a thread of flax well made, tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then hold it, and do not stop straining the thread of flax until it presses the artery, and feels working; and if the roots are thick, be careful to cauterize it by the belly, but you can certainly cauterize half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize so it does not recur; then heal the wound and ensure you do not cover the ulcer that is of fox color and weak sensation and milky gaze.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of the scrofula hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts forth
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of the wound or tear of a fistula and is on the abdomen and in some cases of boils as it happens in other routes or blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is through the break of the sack and the exit of the boil, its color resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the intestine's opening, then it is more diverse; and when you press it with your hands, it repulses, and returns, and possibly becomes hardened, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is light and easily open when you press with your hand, do not force it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a certain amount.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to swelling, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you observe whether its appearance is due to the blood of an artery or vein, or swelling.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You must let the treatment be. For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is due to the intestines or feces, you must command the patient to strain their bowels and stretch out straight, then press down all around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command him to lie down between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area that you have pointed out with a spatula.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then place half of the abscess on top of a large spoon.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie him tightly with a strong thread or a strong silk cord, and bind his hands securely.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open half of the abscess extended on the tendon, and put your index finger in it, and seek the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the tendon, loosen it, and push the intestine out of the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bubble, grasp it at its base, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein becomes obstructed, go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two thin wires through them, and place the needles in a cross shape where you made the incision to pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then pinch the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, pull out the needles, and leave the place until it can, and let the flesh rot by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when it becomes tender and can be pierced, then treat as necessary, and cut open the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as necessary, and stitch up the place;
dou chancre	two boils
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	In the division we said the resemblances of boils, and how to treat them with medicines, and how to remove the cure of iron; and we say boils occur in the flesh, and great caution is required in their treatment, and the ancients said that when boils are in a place where they can be shaved like boils that are on mammary glands, and in the thighs, and similar places, it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it should not be approached, because I never knew anyone to heal them; no one ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, it is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then let him heal if he has manifest repletion, then make the patient sick or healthy one league for the work; then pour your ointment or salve over the boil and shave all around, leaving nothing unshaven; and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood makes you counteract against cutting the artery or vein, cauterize until the wound is staunched; then heal it with another medicine until it heals.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the similarities of hydropisy, and in what manner the accumulation of water is made, and the signs of each semblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only to be treated; and no iron should be touched for these 2 semblances: tympanites and yposarche, because it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this semblance of hydropisy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not work, look to see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides hydropisy, such as swelling of the belly and similar things; do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he has no other disease besides hydropisy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then act thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient upright on your hands, and the assistants press the belly towards the lowest part of the bladder, then take the spatula with sharp points according to this form: And it should be slender in two parts. The point should not be too deep so that it cannot reach the intestine when inserted, and it should not pierce through.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the hernia is directed towards the intestines: if so, you should cut incisions of three fingers' width straight down below the navel, and if the hernia is due to liver disease, it should be on the left side of the navel, three fingers; and if it is due to swelling, it should be on the right side, and the patient should not lie down over the incision so that superfluous fluids do not run to that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin with an instrument, push it out, and place your hand with a spatula between the skin and the sac as when peeling back a layer to a thickness of one nail or less; then pierce the sac until the spatula comes to the place of the fluid, which is the bladder, then pull it out and push this instrument of which there is a picture here: It resembles a thin silver chain, made of tin or light iron, and has four small holes on the underside; one on one side, three on another side, and one on another. The head is shaped like a feather quill, and it's the form of the incision that scribes cut the quill pen with:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	On the top above is the anus, so that when the instrument reaches the bladder, you should now push down on the instrument. Void it then either halfway or one-third of it, for if you look at more than necessary in this hour, it may happen by chance that the patient dies due to resolution of their spirit from the weapon, or they fall unconscious, or they come close to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But in emptying according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the power mean for the patient and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the juice, and it is now held back by the coagulant that stops the bleeding which is on the vein, as I have spoken, that you pierce in this way; then repeat the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering this, and draw a small amount of juice from it;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day and be careful not to let it stay but only a little juice. If you doubt about the patient and leave too much juice, heal it with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint with wine; heal it with drying medicines until it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the spleen after the extraction of the juice, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the wound
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Occasionally, children are born who have no or small foreskins in the penis, or they are not in their proper position. If it is necessary, it should be pierced immediately with a very thin cannula such as this: then put a thin silk thread of flax into the foreskin and tie it and keep it for 2-4 days, until it wants to urinate; if it is removed, urinate, and then replace it. However, it should not be necessary in this case, as the urine that comes out does not close it.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the foreskin is small, it should be treated with flax thread as we have said, and it will expand. Those who do not have a foreskin at the tip of the penis are bladder-stones, for no one is born with a foreskin at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they stretch their penis; and they cannot enjoy sexual intercourse due to this because the matter cannot reach the opening, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is that the patient lies on their back with the head of the penis and the bottom in the same position as a pen, so that the foreskin can open in the middle, as needed; beware of blood flow that often comes, and if it happens, stop the bleeding by applying pressure to the affected area and treating the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this albatross appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of foul genitals; there are both malicious and non-malicious ones; you must catch them once a week with subtile ointment, pick and clean all of them, then put soft cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top, then treat with diaphinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the albatross is malicious, with a putrid color and discharge, then you must bring cautery. When you have picked it, and if the albatross is in the root of the penis and has both an internal part and an external part, then you must remove the internal albatross first; and when it is sewed up, you cure the external one. For when you treat them together, the genitals are not secure from being pierced, and there comes blackness and corruption in the penis and where it was; you must chew everything that is black and corrupted, then put it on top of the poultice of honey and flour made of pumpkin seeds and sometimes, then treat with other cures until it is healed.
