Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, bring the lunar cautery as follows: The cauteries assist in two ways together: for bleeding and for corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must apply or lead a sheath of plank, and make the patient urinate; and when the skin becomes loose at the tip of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you should shave with one instrument, until the ligaments are separated, and release the head of the penis from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then shave with one spatula or knife very close to the tip of the penis and skin; then separate very carefully between two fingers, and put a thin linen cloth dampened in cold water on it so that it does not become exposed again.
de la circoncision	circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply the healing of wounds like other injuries; however, when we perform this work at our will and specifically on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and make it as easy to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say circumcision for their children in the old days because it was not in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision around .i. day, and the strong, and in all cases a novice; however, the cowards because there are two pieces of cloth, and by chance if one above is cut off and it remains the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it should be covered, and the pain is double; and in amputation, which is near the tip of the member, there is no assurance of healing; and in amputation of the nail by chance the iron escapes, ruins the work, and many times there is such a need for amputation that there is no need for amputation.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the amputation made at the ligament of sinew, I have found the benefit of experiment, for the saw cuts equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you should cut equally in every direction; but that the sinew be well straightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you do not tie the sinew only, but rather to loosen it in all possible ways.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make it be between your hands straight, and put strength between your hands or under your feet so the infant does not see, nor any of the tools; then push your hand to the vein and blow or sigh, and pull it up until the head of the vein is out; then clean it well of the filth that has assembled there, then tie the place signified with a double thread, then tie it under one knot to another loop; and hold it at the second knot by the thumb and index finger, and twist between the loops, then quickly untie the knot and pull the chief of the vein.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the blood come out drop by drop, for it is the pus; put powder on top and on top of the powder, one cloth glued with a mixture of cooked egg white steeped in rose water, compounded with fresh rose oil, let it stay until the next day, and cure it with other medicine until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and they should be as large as the fists equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the vein within is cut open; then it must be stretched with your fingernail so that the wound festers over; and press it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take tweezers, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If it lasts for three days and what is under the penis is swollen, let it be until the abscess subsides, and the wound scabs over; then press gently as you can move it, and keep away from the part of the penis, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the limb with things beneath a wound of powder, as we have said or treating powders, and if you press too hard beyond measure, it will go above; then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or cheese, or similar things, as we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that retention is caused by a stone in the bladder, then the patient must be bent over his knees; and he should put his feet on the back, and extend his abdomen from the part above the lower back, and hold the patient as tightly as possible; and then the bladder neck is compressed to expel the stone upward, so that the urine is relieved.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", which is as follows: it should be made of thin delicate silver tube, like a bird's feather; and its neck should be about half a palm long and subtle at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of urine release is that you take one double thread, tie one end to the top of a linen or cotton cloth and push the top of the thread into the syringe; then pull off the excess lining and push it up to the top of the syringe, then oil or butter and egg white are applied to the syringe, and the patient is seated on one chair, and their bladder and penis are rubbed with moist oil of olive and cold water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then double the penis up towards the anus; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and make the patient feel like they are coming to an empty place, and this is not done according to this order for any other reason except that the one guiding it or where it goes is twisted; then the thread is pulled out little by little, and the urine follows the lining, then remove the thread, and correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scratches or blood comes in the bladder, or pus is assembled there, and you see it exuding acids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the levers are set so that the medicines flow out in such a way that they stop the penis well without addition, if it can draw out moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you wish to administer your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the caster in the moisture, and pull gently along its length; if you pull the moisture towards the caster, and then push strongly along its length; it will enter the caster, and reach the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle enema used to enema the bladder: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or copper and has the head higher than one thumb or the fingers; below this is one sheep's bladder or linen; then take a goat's bladder and put in the moisture that you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between two thumbs using a good thread doubled; and heat one end of the moisture over fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture approaching, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle, pierce it roundly around; then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like one would assemble a thimble and put inside that which you see of oil and moisture and water, tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press it with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the section on stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have told the difference between a stone embedded in the rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work in size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it opens the urinary passage, and increases the pain of the patient's penis, and it pierces many times, and then twists; and from these jumps the foundations are weakened; and children's healing is light until they have 4 years, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is a medium ailment for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to clean the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out upwards; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downwards; then search for it and touch it with your fingers;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut it on the stone. And if it does not fall with a touch all around, moisten your left index finger, if the patient is an infant, or use oil, if the patient is an adult who has completed his development; and place it on its base, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it towards the bladder's neck; then press on it and push it to the side where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and order him to extend his right hand upward and remove the skin below the scrotum in the part where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, thus forming the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make an incision between the scrotum and the base, not on the left side but along the right side of the nail; let it be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be close to its base, and the cut should be wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large:
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure must be applied which is the foundation, so that it leaps without labor; and know that there is this stone or angle, and edges: it is broken out; and if there is this one which is swollen, similar to a plum, and rounded, from where the dislocation occurs, it is to be expelled.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Then, where there are edges and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not leap, then you must pull up with tweezers which are like a limer at the top, to forcefully draw out the stone so that it does not escape; or you push underneath with a thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot manage it in this way, you widen .i. small hole, and without cutting, pull it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, push the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then hit it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be broken into smaller pieces, and a larger wound must be made. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes immediately through the place where the lees cannot seal; but still you should make an effort to pull it out, or break it with tweezers, until you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, hold it together, and place a damp cloth in oil and wine on top, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie down on his neck, do not undo the bindings until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you undo it (the bindings), wash it well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment defyfikon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If an abscess or rotting occurs in the wound and congealing of blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in this manner without passing: then insert your finger into the wound, extract the blood, because if it remains, it will rot the bladder and destroy it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then clean the wound thoroughly and gently with water and linen, and aid in all possible ways until it heals; and it is necessary that all the herbs you use for healing, you bind the patient's legs together, and apply the medicine on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is lodged in the urinary passage and cannot be expelled; treat as I will say next, you cut many times, excuse yourself from cutting due to this treatment. I have proven this before.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the following shape and pierced at four angles into one thread:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the stone beneath the bladder, so that it cannot return into the bladder; then gently push the awl into the stone; and turn the awl bit by bit in the stone until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon after the urine will come out, then press your hand on what is retained inside the stone that is within the bladder. Soon it will be broken, and it will burst forth with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread around the stone and another above, then direct the awl towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, remove the lower thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone (of women)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is embedded in a woman, and if it ever occurs, it is a great trouble for the healer, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that there is the possibility that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that it cannot be found a woman skilled enough to reveal herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	The third reason is that sometimes it cannot be found a woman skilled enough in this art; and the fourth reason is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of a man, therefore it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If you find it necessary, then you must take a woman skilled in this art and if she is hard to find, do not hesitate to use one chaste maiden; and present a wise woman as bailiff or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to make the incision of the stone that you command.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then you must insert your finger or base and search for the stone; and if you find it, you should press it down with your finger under its base, and advise her to push her hand or the sick person with her left hand on the bladder formed.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If you find it (the stone), she should move it little by little from the opening of the bladder downwards to its root, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone in the root of the thigh near the cervix, where it is moved, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move your finger above or below the stone, and cut it at first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then bring the patient's thigh, if you feel the stone, press the wound so that the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many kinds of stones: for example, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges. Know their appearances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone pierces through [the skin], put vitriol powder on it and hold for an hour until it is cauterized; then return to your work, until the pain subsides, and have the tools I told you about in the extraction of the stone, to help you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the bone pierces through [the skin], it is because an artery has been cut; put powder on it and bind with tents and bandages, do not continue this, but leave the stone alone and do not extract it, or the patient may die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the wound heals, then return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of a flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	An aquous hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "white pus", and sometimes it is specifically within the egg's membrane, if one believes that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the bladder between the white pus we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and it spreads out this matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the bladder, and this moisture can have several colors: either it descends to yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white and smooth as we have said, it is an abscess, that is, long like an egg, and does not open the eyes, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very cloth, it is an abscess with part of an egg, and for this reason, one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the eyes and the white smooth part, one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe it all around with the instrument, so that you understand its form, as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intromission (procedure), judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron (fire cautery), it is necessary that the patient should be anesthetized to the extent of our power and filling of his body; then lay him on his back, upon a thing slightly raised, and put many layers of cloth underneath him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then lie on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the probe to one of the two costal regions near the joint.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and pierce the skin of the joint along its length until reaching the nail; and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the joint up to a white line, and peel off the thin layer according to your power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the wound deeply with a wide lancet, extract all the liquid, then place your fingers, and hold the wound open from above; do not touch the cartilage of the nostrils but only the wound itself. Cut through the ribs carefully so that it is done skillfully or else the liquid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg jumps out of your work (during the procedure), reset it in its place when you have completed the wound treatment with the lancet; then join the two ribs at the cartilage of the nostrils with a stitch, and treat the wound as other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then you must bind the vessels that are suspended with caution to prevent bleeding; then cut the cartilage completely and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the wound is divided into two parts together, know that it are two branches; if you cut the other part like you have done the first equally, then squeeze out the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put more linen moistened in wine and oil on it, and put on the two wounds, and put cloths doubled over it, and tie it all up with the bandage that is in this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths and use linen thread according to this pattern and sew them together into the belt of the braces, and one of the wounds takes it on the bottom up to the back, and the other at the part of the thumb; and the other two wounds take the other ends, and gather all the rest together in the buckle of the bracer.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes medicine is this ramice of fire in the place of iron's thickness, and you take .i. cautere cultellaire subtil (a thin cautery knife), and press the skin with it, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the pus at one point, and peel off the skin with this thin heated cautery;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And press in all ways as you can, until everything is heated; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg (yolk); and know that this work is more beneficial; and pay attention to avoiding the flow of blood, and do not perform surgeries at the joints;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if no thing opposes you, or abscess boil or running of blood or other such thing, then heal what opposes you, as stated earlier.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work because of its dreadfulness, you should perform a perforation as I tell you; and it is that when you are sure by the signs we have mentioned that the dislocated joint is on the left side,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Make the patient sit on a raised seat; then perforate the abscess in the part below the whole spur, and place the perforation along the length of the body; and let the openings be wide, so that all the pus can flow out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then place cotton on the joint, hold it in place, and let the remaining water drain out, then heal until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white linen cloth does not allow the water to flow from the wound's mouth, you must insert a reed or an instrument used to treat the water of dropsies (as described previously) into it; then widen the wound by 1 inch, ensure that the water returns, and wait for 6 months or thereabouts, and when the water is collected as described earlier, the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cheek
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this treatment there is fear in many positions, therefore it seems to me that one should leave [the patient] in those positions.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially from the bowels; and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is due to an excess of sour and acid fluid that spreads to the bowels or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; it does not hurt, but it is a serious abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes an abscess is painful and hard, of the same color, and sometimes it comes from an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to an artery, it can be recognized by the hot and painful position of the abscess when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	A person who is affected by swelling of the vein can be recognized by his characteristic signs on the touch of the fingers,   (or, "A person suffering from swelling in a vein can be identified by the manifestations displayed upon touching the fingers.")
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can easily make an incision on this appearance, and on other signs. (or, "and can easily perform an incision on such symptoms, and on others.")
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the kernel of the cyst, then the egg is in the upper part, and the thread is very white and free, and release the suspension from all parts of the egg.  (or, "It requires cutting the core of the cyst, with the yolk located at the top, and the thread being very white and unattached, and releasing the contents from all parts of the egg.")
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already softened with these hatchlings born, then you should pull out the egg and crush it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is sour in the yolk, or within the vessels (inside the egg), you must deliver all that tender part, and crush it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the shell is on one side, you must crush it completely, and pull out the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply the wound with dampened wool in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the eyes
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling resembling a boil, with the softening of the eyes.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient grows silent when he goes;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	And the treatment for this disease is as dangerous as it is necessary.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	Nevertheless, we shall tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You must make the patient sit on a raised seat, then place the support for the loins below the waist.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To every vessel which is near to the penis, touch them the masters, and stretch them out properly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then pierce the sharp lancet broad across the vessels until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then peel them from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert an awl with a double thread and tie it to the first place where blood has come out, and then tie it to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then strike the limbs straight, according to the length of the body, and expel the corrupt moisture from them.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as with other treatments where you apply a poultice, so that no worms emerge from either of the corners.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because by doing this, there is no harm, and if all the worms appear visible, it is necessary to draw out the corners of all the wounds.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their sperm due to the incisions of the worms, and dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the hernia
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The consequences of this hernia are by the incision or herniotomy, or extension on the abdomen in the area of the inguinal region, which causes the intestines to descend from that rupture towards one of the groins.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this hernia is either by the herniotomy or extension of it, and these are the two ways in which it may occur due to various causes: either by impact, or jump, or strain, or lifting heavy objects, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is of the extension of the disease, are such that they occur little by little, in a long time, and do not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And abscesses are equal up to the full point, because the disease follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is of the section of the disease, are such that they cause sudden pain at the beginning and abscesses appear different, close to the skin surface, which is due to the outflow of intestines and the body turning away from the disease.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines come out of the circles and are retained there, causing great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, which causes one to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	The method of the work is that you instruct the patient to draw out the intestine with their hand from within the wound if it can be inserted.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then place it on its neck between your hands and lift the legs.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then cut the skin above, and slice the whole hide of the hocks with length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then insert your fingers into the groin area according to what you need to open the wound, and make them so that the bones can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape off the fat that is under the hide of the hocks until the white fat is entirely exposed from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then insert your index finger into the area behind the hock, between the white fat that is under the hide of the heel, and the second fat.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And separate the one that is behind the eye, and enter the second syphac; then move your right hand within the cavity of the skull, and place the white syphac towards the top at your left hand, and lift the eye to the whole syphac towards the tailbone.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	Instruct the minister to extend the eye upwards, and release that which is in front behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	If you find that the intestine is rolled up or hard white syphac, bring it to the abdomen.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take an awl with one thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it in the back part of the sacrum, which is after the skin of the coccyx; after the loin, then cut the heads that appear from the threads, until there are four strands left;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the sacrum, which we have said is beneath the skin of the coccyx, with a strong thread of two strands;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Wrap the threads around the heads and tie them with a thread of two strands so that no one who cares for them can enter into it, except arrows cannot come out;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And set the ligature straight according to the first long ligament, and after these two ligaments leave the suture that is under the cartilage of the knee, the great one by a thumb's width.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	Then according to the roundness that the egg carries; then strike in the part that is under the skin of the knee, as much as it needs, and bend it, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply wet wool in oil and put it on wounds, and bring the ligament that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes, the whites (of the eyes) are cauterized as we have said, after incision, due to fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For there are often instances when the ligament (of the eyelid) remains closed; if it takes too long to fall down, it should be gently washed with hot water, and what we have said applied to it until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then treat the wound with another cure until it heals perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of a meaty hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a remedy that is composed of iron, in such a way that you tie the vessels, above the wound gently below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you press it in the middle and treat the abscess of those who open it, until the vessels bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	"At times rupture comes in the abdomen, as we have said, and open the flanks; and do not remove any of the intestines through the anus, and if it is removed, it is a little bit, and repair them every hour;"
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	"Moreover, if it remains too long at that point, the wound or the hernia swells as the intestines are expelled;"
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	"This happens due to the extension of the hernia in the abdomen, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then the flanks become soft and swollen and open;"
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes the cure is by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And have the patient lie supine on his back between your hands, then strike the swelling at the wound with a three-finger width.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then remove the scab that is under the skin, then take the iron and place it on the visible part of the scab.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the center of the abdomen, then count the two levels appearing above the navel, and count them both;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull the head of the arrow, and do not cover it or extend the sheath nor anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal worms;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then heal by the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the threads, if it becomes infected and heals the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swollen member has no appearance in the wound, and the fire cautery is applied here, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the swelling on the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the genitals becomes swollen in some men due to softening of the testicles, and it appears like pus; and when one sees it needs to be cured, you must make the patient lie down on his back, and strike the swollen skin on top of the natural skin; then bring together the two lips at a stitch, and if you see, first sew the excess skin swollen part in 3 or 4 firm stitches; then strike between the stitches, and the cure is like other wounds until it heals, and the thread the skin.
dou chastrement	The punishment (or treatment)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The chapter speaks of two kinds of punishment or treatment (chastremens) mentioned in our law, of which one is when the mirrors answer concerning the treatment, and the other, because we often need to punish certain animals for our assistance, such as cows, sheep, pigs, and others. I say therefore that chastremens is performed in two ways: by attraction or by cutting. In the one we perform on the animal, we seat it in hot water until the joints are softened; then we grab them with our hand, keeping it pressed until they return to their original position and no longer feel painful. The treatment of cutting (chastrement de taille): you must dye the animal, press the skin of the joints with your left hand, attach a rope, and strike above each limb with one blow when you have sufficiently scorched them; leave a small amount of fat and the subtle fat that is on the vessels; this kind of punishment is more severe than the one performed by attraction because sometimes there remains something in the joints due to attraction, which makes the animal desire lust. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites (or intersex individuals)
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways among humans: one, when there are openings between the two genitals like a woman's figure by nature, where there is hair and sometimes urine from the urethra. And the other way is in women, who have something above the penis as a rod and two genitals. The treatment for man and woman is to treat all adjacent wounds as with other wounds; however, in the second case, of men whose urine jets through the skin of the genitals, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	the tentigen
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The cautery with fire instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de erratique	The cautery with fire instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is the nature of women that is not delivered or lost; it can be by birth or accident due to disease; or it is due to growth or swelling that occurs inside a woman, or outside, wherever it may be; and it should be prevented, and the conception, and possibly the flowers to grow. The knowledge of such things is by observing the behavior of the belly. If the discharge is close to appearing, whether in your hand or at your right side, hasten and press as follows: place your two hands together, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then form the fingers, so that the subtle swelling is round, and the discharge opens. Then take flax, wet it with oil, and lay it over the area, and let the woman rest at home every day, so that it does not heal. And if the swelling is soft and subtle, and it is close to two levers, you should hurry, and press as follows: place your two hands together again, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then form the fingers, so that the subtle swelling is round, and the discharge opens. Then take a linen cloth and pour oil over it, and lay it over the area, and let the woman rest at home every day, so that it does not heal. And if the swelling is hard and large, you must cut it with a spatula resembling the leaves of myrtle. If the discharge is from a growth, you should squeeze it with onions and cut it; and have medicines stained with blood, such as cinnamon, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then bring a large wooden spoon, so that the wound does not heal; and let it be long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other remedies until it heals. And when in the woman there is a growth, you must cut it according to this method, unless it is an enchanted abscess in the woman. For the enchanted abscess that is in the woman should not be touched.
des emorroides	The diarrhea
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For hemorrhoids without full evacuation, which is not usually treated with cautery, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become swollen; and we have said in the division what their likenesses are, and signs, and I will say here those that respond to cure. I say that hemorrhoids and the swelling, when they are fully in the anus, and cannot be felt, may not be cured with iron. Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that may be cured. Therefore, it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then let the swelling be tied up with pincers near the roots, then sprinkle medicines stopping blood on it, such as camphor and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press its feet to the outside for an hour, then put it in hot ice; and if bleeding comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grapefruit peel and holly and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on its back. And if it bleeds, that is good. If not, let it be pierced with blisters on the back and at the breasts without iron; then take linen, and moisten it in the juice of plantain or elderberry with old wine, and let it heal at the place. And when the abscess rests, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles one sharp head, which must be covered as I said for the swelling; and then let it heal until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of treating an abscess come in marriage (meaning the body), such as boils, abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the section on classification. Therefore, it is necessary for me to speak about the hot abscess that comes in marriage, which is not one of those boil-like abscesses; and if you wish to know how to treat it with iron, observe whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its occurrence, full of heat and fever, and turns red if possible. Do not rush to pierce it, but let it heal until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat or two seats where he can lean, support his back, place his feet in the direction away from the leg, spread his legs apart, tie them with a strong cord, then bring the needle towards the right side of the abscess, and introduce the instrument used to open the abscess, from which the form will follow. It is necessary that when you see this instrument introduced, you pierce the base first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not irritate it; it is also necessary that you place the nozzle of the instrument above, and mark the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and it becomes soft in your hand, it should be covered with linen or a clean, damp cloth; when the boil is empty, you should put moistened wool soaked in rose oil or green, dry, cooked oil into the wound; place the soaked wool on the bottom of the abscess and on top of the abscess and on the handle of the linen a clean, damp cloth that has been cooked with vinegar or malves (a type of plant); then heal it after two days with ointment, until it is healed; sometimes the abscess and wound are lifted by enema with water and honey, and then with water or long-cooked lily roots and aristolochia, then return to the ointment. And if the wound has returned in the abscess, it is necessary for you to avoid using fire, but treat it as we have said in the section on classification.
de l’enfantement	childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	1st sentence: It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman laboring downward, and desire to smell the anus; then the child should hasten to be born; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it issues forth from under its head, and follows it with itself; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on the woman's abdomen, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it pushes against her head, it follows it, and the husband sheds his superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes upon its feet, or the body or the head, or the hands, or upon the abdomen, or the backside, and is converted perhaps on its neck, and by other evil figures; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these matters, and be aware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out from under its head naturally and the woman gives birth with difficulty and her strength is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then apply to her nature oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the midwife between her hands the small spatula of which this form is:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the afterbirth, and press its edge with a nail until the moisture that is inside it comes out; and hold the woman's belly until the child pushes down, and if it does not push, you must cleanse her with musk-scented fenugreek oil and castor oil; then make her take and vomit condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour; thus this will help the child be born. And if two hands come out, you must gently straighten them bone by bone; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on one saddle, lift her legs up; then turn the saddle onto the ground, and bind her so that she does not move at the turning; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here before, and extract the child, and straighten it as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the birth of the child on its feet
