et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and it turned out to be nothing, but he improved in better condition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they said to any experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm grips on large pliers, then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the pliers have opened the mouth, place it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it pulls its mouth open.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	And then grip the head (of the patient), and hold it so that it cannot dislocate.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then apply another force after that in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely seized.
et cout la plaie.	and stitch (or suture) the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head (of a dislocated joint) is re-set in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	And it can be tied the intestine with a thin string which is cut from the intestine of an animal.
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread from the intestine that is quite sharpened,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread a thin twisting linen string.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then thread the wire on the needle, sew the intestine, and draw it through the incision.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of stitching wounds is not beyond what can be done with faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy nor health, except by skillfulness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or ...
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it swells, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and moreover when it bursts and releases fluid.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth, a hard and white nodulation that causes no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is swollen like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes in clear jump, and other times thick bowed.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes shallow, and other times quite deep.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have spoken about it in the section on wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	It can only be through one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	It is to know, by the little wound or body.
ou por sa malice;	or by its illness.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within and above the lips that does not allow flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or if there is too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	If the limb is fractured, and the substance is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	if the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because in that region, digestion is slow and health slows down and becomes weaker by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	There are veins or bones here.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, the signs, and the remedies of medicines in divisions.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you the cure for a fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulae (abnormal passages) coming from great veins, arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the anus, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to one of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all such fistulas are of severe healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance to remedy them.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	If there is any fistula that does not reach the level I mentioned, and you are confident of its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and examine it to determine if it is straight. If the fistula is straight, puncture it with a tent of pitch or iron.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	If the fistula is twisted, search for a thin probe made of wood.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the plaster (bandage) bends itself around the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula (abscess or wound) is pierced with fingers and you cannot find it well by probing,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	If the clisterium (the lower part of the uterus) is punctured by one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	Because moisture is short from one place to another, and purifies it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then pierce it cautiously to your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is completely healed,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where it is located;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the location of it, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the joints I have mentioned, if the shoulder follows as I have said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and break open the fracture and the rotten bones that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then care for it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	if the wound is well penetrated in a straight direction, you must cut through it as deep as possible,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then he puts moistened bandages in the treatment of ague, and thrusts them into the mouth of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medication erodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts salves with clean fat, until it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	if it is not healthy by this means, then cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted by a fistula, strike it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve does not trouble you or your main limbs as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, strike it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal with things that are healthful until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	And if [the patient] is not healthy, bend [the limb] as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the font (spring/source):
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you dig and excavate as much as possible to reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	remove all the corruption, then reset it (the affected part) in its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it (the dislocation) is thus settled, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this isn't so, know that the corruption is too advanced, and you cannot achieve anything in it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to let it heal naturally.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corruption, and you can extract it with the pliers
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	If it is dislocated by some instrument,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are several bones, pull them all out, do not leave any one of them;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and press, moisture, and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove [them] within an hour, place something stimulating [or irritating] pusiferous on the wound.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	Let the flesh grow around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	then the bones will be more easily set.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone such as the thigh or the leg,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	Let the king press down on the corruption only until all the blackness is expelled.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is much corruption and it reaches the bone marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to be cut all the way to the corruption and then treated until it heals.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you about a fistula that happens to one man in his leg, [or]
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you take an example and aid in your work. [or]
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something coming from within his body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	The matter kept coming to the leg, and a large abscess was drained without any reason to open it further.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	However, due to their foolishness, they opened the abscesses too much.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they dug out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many pustules formed that all exuded pus and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many patients were cured around two years without any skilled surgeon present.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	As long as I was summoned to him and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which ran through the wounds with great pain.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the chest of the young man became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent at one of the wounds, and then searched all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	And I found that they come together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	Then I hurried and cut into one wound until I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was convinced that the bone was corrupted and thought there was no other corruption except what I had left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And begins to treat the wound with salves for long times, but cannot heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	Then continues, and uncovers the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found continuous corruption in the bone, and burned it, and then left it to heal on its own;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not cover more than a palm of the bone, and the wound festered all over,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	Then heal with medicine; it will quickly become healthy and strengthened.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because it often evacuated blood, but it became entirely healthy.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And a hard cyst was born in the place of the bone, and it was well-placed and had no harm or adverse effect whatsoever, neither at the side nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take a ligature, and tie it to the end of the open bone fragment,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	And command anyone to extend it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	And tie another string of linen larger than the first one and attach it above the cartilage that is detached from the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And extend the head, so that you draw the rotten cartilage downward;
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And uncover the flesh over the joint where you want to be, let it not blister the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put one iron or a plaster under the bone to heal the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	It is necessary to be as much as can be seen and felt [the corruption], and be there again later.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt but does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	If you uncover the flesh entirely; then put one splinter beneath.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and when the corruption is between the parts, let the thread be of the length of the corruption, one finger width, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and let the bone be on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut it (the affected part).
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or the foot, it is very severe.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but in any case, you must investigate this corruption, how it has opened.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that there are many different cutting tools and saws to cover the bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	for this reason, it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the tool needed, according to knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the signs of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you consider the instrument which is needed according to what is required of it.
dou feu	cautere de
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder joint may dislocate from within or from without.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried this corrosive treatment with the medicines, but it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	It is necessary to cover that member up to where corruption starts.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient shivers because of death or a greater evil, which is a defect in the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs that the member turns black as if it were burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then comes the corruption of one member to another.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the sting of certain venomous creatures such as sea-scorpions and vipers and the like.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the throat of the neck, strike it, and give it no opportunity to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, strike at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And there is no use in applying foreign substances except for the amount of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do this in the same way when corrosion comes or putrefaction: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or strikes, strike all the blow.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it rises in the leg, strike at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy for the patient but to weaken him with death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	The method of striking or treating a limb is that you tie it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And extend one minister to the lower link, and another minister to the upper link.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	Then you desire the cartilage that is between the two links at one spanile wide space, as long as the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then take the hide or silk and put on each side one linen cloth so that the silk does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And come to the patient with other wounds and abscesses dressed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when bleeding occurs during your work, quickly cauterize the area.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	and you place some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	tie the limb with a covenable rope, and heal it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in the city of Piet:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	It happened to him a black spot that seemed burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion first attacked his tooth at the root, until it consumed all the tooth;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he immediately covered the tooth with copper, and it became healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and a long time later the corrosion returned to his hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I place him on things causing rebound after the purification of the body, but the corruption cannot cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And you command me to cauterize (burn) his hand, and I do not want that unless I have hope of making it better.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And also doubted that if I am cutting off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the human was weak; and he gave up all hope and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And if it (the patient) strikes with a sword his hand, and it becomes wounded;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have no other purpose for relating this except that you do otherwise if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess sometimes occurs in a charnut (probably a type of joint), and it remains for so long that it causes a great swelling of the body.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they (the doctors) run and pierce, and jump on the swelling, and the wound opens up, as a knight does.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin on top is as thin as a single linen cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it will not reach to the bone or to the nerve, and such illness is called "putrid".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is long enough to reach the bone completely, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the cook who is to do this task, you are to wrap him all over, and in the same manner when it becomes thin, just like a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And let it not be cut away for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	If you have the belief that the skin is rotten and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if the skin is thick with flesh, you should cook it with clyster in this manner:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if the breasts are large, and if the ones within them have a strong-smelling discharge.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then, administer the Egyptian enema medicine as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take equal parts of asafetida, oil, and litargirio; cook them in one vessel over fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take from these as needed, and make it into vinegar and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and anoint the breast and constrict the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by straining;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this frequently until the breast is purified and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take vine charcoal ashes, and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let the bleeding continue, and cleanse with leeches, until you know that the wound is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor ash water.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and the cleansing with water and honey or a little litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you cleanse it with honey and sweet wine, which the honey has the property of purifying and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine made it stronger.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this, and you are certain that the breasts have been properly cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clusterization of those causing it to produce pus in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you take emplastrum of definite amount, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clusterize them with certain medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken of their properties or treating the wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the wound of the breast is small and the cannula of the cautery cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	and makes a small wound with a blade, and puts on it an Egyptian ointment bandage,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and apply basilicon oil, spread it out widely.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, make it narrow to leave only enough space for a finger or a plaster to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the hernia protrudes above, push it down or lower it to its level.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the hernia is full, do not let any flesh enter into it;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	If the arm is arranged so that the elbow bends as low as it can go.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the arm is fully straightened, do not allow anything to pierce the flesh there.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast under as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If the arm moves in such a way: that the bone moves slightly downward without anything being left of the bone;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to place on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch over it a linen cloth that covers the whole breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then apply the force to the sore on the breast, just a little larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	The hinges are anointed with oil or another cloth according to the amount of wounds.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the wound over the chest to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one who is on the wound over the chest, removes it frequently to remove the bone,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And learn what kind of bone is moving, whether it is poisoned or bruised, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see the pus rising from the breast wound,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is hardened, approach the healthy part;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then in the morning or later in the day, when you open the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	If a bandage or dressing is changed and renewed.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast sags down improperly after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons circulate after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the healing approaches. For there are men whose wounds delay in healing and those who act contrary to this;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and bends unhealthily out of joint from the breast after many days, knowing that breasts do not straighten themselves;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts remain swollen and are protracted, apply medicines that dry moisture in substance but are moist in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as I have determined, for there is great part of vitriol and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take an ointment made with rose oil and equal parts of old wine as a base.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then let it set and use it; this same method works better when heated and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when the prescribed ointment is not available,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	And then apply a cloth (drapel), place it on the chest, and sometimes an Aristotle's sage (long-term treatment) is administered.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lilies, which is also like flour of vetch and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simple or compound medicines: grind them, make into powder, put on the honey that I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the patient is wounded, and not treated by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	therefore learn that corruption enters fully, and causes pressure in the bone, or hard members, or joints;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pancreas is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	and may arise in other fingers by chance.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed and no care is taken, one abscess will follow another.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and throw boil ointment until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance, it may reach the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corrosion up to the bone, until pain smells, and the chest is wide, and the color becomes pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must cut into it. Remove all the excess that remains from the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is clean.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail follows the flesh closely, and starts to become swollen, and begins to pus,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	You must put the ointment under the nail so that it does not touch the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And push up the bone, and strike the cartilage softly and gently.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And place on top of the remaining cartilage, the remains of burning and corrosive medicine to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw it out, because as much as the bone becomes corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see a bone to correct, strike it with a hammer as mentioned before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	heal it until it is sound;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	if it is wounded and swollen and causing great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	strike the joint with a sharp spatula in a transverse cutting motion above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And watch that the incision does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, place something on top to alleviate [the pain].
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the injured hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The swelling that arises in some men's hands by accident is entirely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And by chance there is a tooth or bones, and sometimes it has a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And from some of these, nails grow in the root of the joint, or the growth is in certain fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The nail that grows in any finger does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And the nail that grows at the joint of the finger may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The girth of a fat person is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the circumference at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint should be treated carefully, cover him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In a newborn or one whose navel remains, you must first cover the round cartilage up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bind the bone with an appropriate splint, then let it heal until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously the swellings that come to the joints arise by birth, or by injury from a wound, or by burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must bind that swelling so that it can heal according to its natural shapes.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two dampened or wet linen cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two thin planks until the joints are welded, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If any of its bones come together with the palm, then strike the weld as needed.
Des vils	Peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These are large veins swollen with melancholic waste that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it often happens in legs of those who walk and work more than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of the gall, and then heal from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is to strike it, and black blood will be drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein and let all the blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The waist is to be treated in this manner: First, roast the leg in very hot water until the flesh becomes soft.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then hold the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut open the vein in one, two or three places, making a large incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then drain the black blood from your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength allows;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and instruct the patient to bind themselves with black-colored meats.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And repeat the evacuation and sanitation when veins are full, which helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The swelling is handled in this manner: raise the sick person's leg if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then immerse [it] in hot water and raise the leg until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no hot water, heat it with fire, and then press it against the vein along the thigh or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then peel back the skin and scrape the vein from both sides until it appears when it is felt.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And it will become red and black, and when it enters the skin it resembles a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then push the joint underneath (or inside), as long as it is swollen with skin, and then gently bend it to the angle.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then strike it into another place three fingers away; then cut the skin over the vein as far as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then tie up the joint again, as you did, and bend it to another angle, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then cut another piece, or more if needed, then tie it, and bind it at the ankle.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw and empty up to the second joint; then pull it out of joint by joint, until it comes out entirely, then hit it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and lift it, push an awl with a single very strong double thread into it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and draw it out and pull it straight, then push a rod under it, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And guard that it does not bruise, for if it bruises, one cannot draw it nor lift it, and it harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it all, place wool soaked in vinegar and oil on the wound site; and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the sight is contracted, twisted, and entwined together, and it is not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you must break it, do so violently, but do not cover it up; draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to pierce the windpipe is curved and does not cut through, but instead it should be used to open up a vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is large-curved, for if it is thin, it would pierce the windpipe, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil windpipe
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is inserted into the legs, in warm places where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground without moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance, it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to rot that comes from beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If it comes within the body serpent-like and extends, insert between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very great swelling,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then change the joints, and begin the vein to come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around it with a piece of wood from one and a half to two feet long, and sew it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wooden piece on the leg, and every time it moves away, you wrap it around the wooden piece again, and sew it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut a part of it and wrap the remainder, do not cover its root, until it all comes out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	If you cut it, it will return into the flesh, cause an abscess and pus or a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it is necessary to treat it little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten fingers.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And once a man came to me whose size was ten palms long, and when you touch it, it bursts out with one pear or puncture, and pierce it all the way through.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Empty everything inside it; and bring medicinal substances with purgative properties to the place, administer them for some days, then treat it as an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein swells again, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or ankle.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes very quickly, and from where it jumps; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body swelling and shrinking.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And he feels well when moving from member to member, until it hurts him where the skin is torn or bruised;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infected by corruption of certain humors such as worms, serpents, lice and roundworms or the abdomen;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its nature, because when it travels through the body, it rises to the head and comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you wish to cure and drain it, one can force it only when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must lie the limb above and below with a strong ligament tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then press on top and draw forcefully, and if it is turned completely into the flesh, and you do not find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you burn with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it causes is that it runs oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming towards or near the oil, hold a bellows beneath it, then strike on top, and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and the patient must use corpse medicine with soluble substances to remove bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and avoid eating unclean meats such as pork and shellfish.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And it moves from member to member; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and showed her arm, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And after that, the eyes rise as if it were a worm towards the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, as living silver when it cuts from one thing to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain spreads from that place and penetrates into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little after, it runs through the whole body until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I saw that it continued to turn around the body repeatedly.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease manifest itself in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had heard that pain often moved from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	But I did not want it at all, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins open.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appeared that constrained windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are debauched and have moist bodies and veins returned.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels such pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	and press on top firmly until the gas confines itself to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the remedy for those who suffer from windiness is similar to pills made of foul substances, such as pill-shaped figs and pillows of serapin, and other similar ones.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse in their shapes and the parts of the body they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of arrows is that some have large points, small ones, blunt, and sharp-edged ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two corners (angles), and of those with joints (lengues), and of those where there are bones broken (pieces).
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And when a bone falls out in any member, it falls in two ways: either in the principal member, the head (cheveit),
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as the brain (cerveil), heart (cuer), liver (foie), spleen (pormon), kidneys (rains), intestines (intestine), bladder (vessie), and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls into any place of these limbs, and the signs of death which I will tell you later appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Then it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes in many situations afterwards.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this bad sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not fully in, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone and the swelling occurs above the brain:
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is about cataract, stone, gravel, and inflammation in the eyes, redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps without force from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps loss of speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the wound with white fluid like pus, and also jumps like burning coal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, keep yourself from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or wounds, is that it is close to the left breast and feels like it has been stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And sometimes the arrow becomes swollen like hair and produces black blood in the court, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, there is doubt that death is sentencing him.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never pierces the flesh is when there is no scum bubbling from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls on the bedclothes, it is dislodged from the small ribs; and it releases great agony and pain and breathes heavily; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, in case something of undigested meat jumps out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or wounds the belly, and it does not burst through the intestinal path, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes the bladder, and it bursts and leaks urine and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, like the hand and arm, neck, shoulder, and collarbone, spine of the back, ribs, pelvis, legs, and similar parts are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, do this instead.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck or pierced the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out from under the ear fat, and it came out without harm to the sense.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And then I played with an arrow that struck in the grease of the oil underneath the paper below,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was inserted, but it could not reach beyond the flesh.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, with a light iron head shaped like an ear; the wound was clean, and no bad accident happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And through the throat pierced an arrow of an Arab, and the arrow had ears (feathers).
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was a barber, and skillfully pulled it out, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow out from a man, who was struck either in the head or abdomen, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, devised a way to draw it out, and extracted it without any adverse event.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if one sees a man who has an arrow stuck into his back or chest, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained within him, and did not break its natural position.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any hindrance in any of its natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And a second man, who was struck by an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	remained like that for a long time suffering great pain; and many other similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And draw an arrow from a man of the princes, the king who was stuck in the snow.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely bent
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been stuck for three days. When I found the wound, it was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I made a subtle probe and did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	He feels a prick and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of an arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a soothing plaster to the affected area, as the wound did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the arrowhead appeared from the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the plaster for many hours, and heal the wound directly, and let the patient stay like that for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrow within his nose for one day; and he tells me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine with my hands for many hours, until it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow that protruded from the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I align in the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow becomes visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed beyond the limits for four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then I cut open the wound that I had pierced with the tweezers, and could not pull it out from either side.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and devise means of instruments, until I had made tweezers well for one day.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to its form that will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treat it and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror judges that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will then restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I will tell you about the extraction of certain arrows:
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you apply your treatment to it, which I am not saying, for books cannot completely grasp it;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can compare it well with little things, and with what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	nine new works, and nine instruments, in the following of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not go into members where they are fixed except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or from which side they enter, or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it will jump out again at times.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out, leave it until the flesh is swollen all around, and the opening is even.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and similarly if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for some days and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce all around with a very fine needle until the joint is opened wide, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head, and goes to one of the cavities of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said to the patient: do not drain it at all, but let it remain equal for some days after.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow reaches so far, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not driven deeper than the bone but does not reach so far,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient remains for some days without any bad accidents, if the device for drawing is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is driven in deep and cannot be withdrawn, administer tourniquets around it as I have told you; then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is inserted into the body where it cannot be seen, seek it thoroughly;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	if it cannot be extracted due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, if the wound is large enough.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	Pull out the arrow, if there are ears in it as they hold.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	Bone out the part which is fastened in by 2 fingers, if you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	Then break or fold the arrow's ears, as much as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And carefully make sure not to break the arrow, but to draw it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do so at once, if the wound around the arrowhead is opened, then draw it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood obstructs you, bring what we have said in its chapter for the cure.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and protect the incision of the nerve and vein, and use devices as you can move to draw out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Or soon or later, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest aid that can be, and if you cannot do so, then place it according to what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, or if it pierces something or the skin is swollen in that place as we see or feel.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then across, as far as the pliers can reach, and then pull it out; if it does not come now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone and expands the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot come out, let it remain for a while, and then continue the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is an arrowhead inside, push it all the way out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it [the shoulder] had fallen, and you wished to administer a remedy, you would give it... one instrument, comb-like.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then strike hard,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is combed, you strike one instrument with pointed entry for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has touched bone, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	If an arrow or spear or in the belly or bladder or side is near and you can cover it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And do not cover the vein and the nerve, then remove it (the foreign object), then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many forms: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the growing hair is like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To point the arrow's tip, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The forms of the tweezers for extracting and for measuring are as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	for wounds on the chest
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins from which one is healed are 31, of which the head is 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: 2 bands that are after the ears, which are called the "doubles 'herbech'".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the 2 visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 2 veins that are in the 2 hollows of the 2 eyes, which are called "aspirations".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	1) And the vein that is on the forehead;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	3) And the two tendons which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	4) And the two veins that are above the mouth on the lips, and these veins are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	5) And the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly drains are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the first is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median is called "fasting" (or "median vein"), and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the laypeople call it "vein of the heart"; and the left or right side is called the basilica.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call it "vein of the abdomen" and it is above the liver.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	This is the one from which blood is drained, which opens clearly above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The saphenous vein is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is beneath the cavity of the left hip bone,
