et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the wrist of the right side; and the vein called "nase", which is at the other wrist,
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and there are three more veins beneath those in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The following sentence translates to: The blood from the veins that are after the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a surgeon, as I tell you, are that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where veins or vessels are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	seek then for its pulse under your hand, and where you feel its pulse, press firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lance, and thrust it beneath the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut the skin and vein well, two fingers deep through it, and make the blood come out as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The translation of this sentence is: "The vein of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is beneficial to migrate/move old."
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swollen, and inflamed eyelids, and in the heart of tears dried-up in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the vein, as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, until both veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feels the pulse beneath your throat, then press on it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Press the artery near the vein at the top of your throat and thrust the lance beneath it.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Press the vein upwards, and grasp it, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a cut to let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your throat on top of the vein for an hour, then put a piece of cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form the ligature and leave it until it heals; and we have spoken of its covering and its dressing, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the head in the ancient diseases of the face, and has migraines, and reddens.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is that the patient twists his neck so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, hold above your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and not until you work with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the fire should not be too sharp; and it should pass through obliquely because the bone is close, and by chance break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The sinews of the two veins that are in the elbows help with the joints and the thumb, and the groin, and the ulna in oil, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of its pain is such that the patient twists his neck in some way, as previously mentioned.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then pass the iron, and let it be the width of a finger, slightly long and wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the iron is thin, it may break; then make an incision for the blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The iron from the neck vein is useful for fever, scabies, and fecal diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If it comes as a migraine and reddens like in the face, and particularly when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the urine if the patient compresses their neck, then holds their penis with your left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long and thrust it into the opening between the two nostrils;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will soon begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far (in) deep, and make the incision for blood according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The boils of the two kidneys help in the treatment of the anus, and the beginning of leprosy, and many diseases, and poisoning, and corruption, and sores, and scabs.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the wound is that the patient strains their neck under both [arms], as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master stand on top of the sick person's head, and the sick person lie on one bed.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein along its length with a small incision, then drain the blood gently or as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then fix another side on the other vein, then undo the ligament, and hold all the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Do not make the patient strangle (it); leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On Cures of Rabbits
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinuses of the veins in the upper lips help to drain into the mouth, and contribute to decay of the gums, fissures in the lips, and teeth problems and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the sinus are to make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is at the right lip and the other at the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are recognized by being black, and by having small veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	touch them both, and if you do not recognize them and you doubt about it,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	touch the larger one of each pair, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The drainage of veins located beneath the tongue assists after the draining of the cephalic [sinus], and it is in the incision of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of draining are that the patient spits into your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks beneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	therefore one and the other [side], but do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins from which we commonly heal are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when pricking with any flame, mirrhin large or subtle olive oil as you cut, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mirrhin flame is very renowned, and it is large as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the large veins full of thick blood that contains thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more finely, and it is for the fine veins to drain the subtle blood that contains yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The draining of the basilica, which is one of the veins, helps with diseases that are in the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And the lord must purge himself thoroughly, and let blood from the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he pierces the artery, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flames must not be pricked, but cut like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, you must force it to open and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if there is no opening in the basilica, or if you pierce the vein in the arm: it opens manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the fire cautery as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to find the location of the vein, it is necessary that you force the arm, that you touch the place until you recognize the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the joint with a needle, then tie the arm, and burn the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware not to hit the artery when you see the joint swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up high like a child's urine and the limb is red and tender, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Therefore, hurry up, put your hand on it for a long time, then move your hand away from the limb when it stops swelling, as this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave the arm alone, and do not move it, let the patient not move it; be fearful, and do not move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the arm is not bled and it swells, and there is no medicine present, then cut open the artery if it is open, for the head of it will recede; bleed the arm.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of plaster, cut it and take one half of it and apply it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the arm is bled, that's good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stitching is not to be hastily done in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the tendon of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The stitching of the vein shall help to treat blood from the head above and internal bleeding below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it consists of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And the lord must turn himself for the nerve that is beneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he inflates it and anoints it with oil, and unfortunately cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument anesthetic; pull on the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sanity of the head helps, because it draws blood from the head, and assists the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to cauterize with olive oil or myrtle fire, because it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, you should seek the least forceful place, and do not exert pressure if it is necessary for the first time, and you should repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the joints swell for some men, how one should act the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the purity is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about purification is that purification is not brought for anything but to maintain health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the incision shall be made in one of the four veins that are close to the skin: namely, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be incised at the beginning of the privy member, in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it should be incised on the first or third day, after two or four hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The treatment of sickness does not have a fixed hour, but when necessity arises, day or night, in every hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to treat children until they are 12 years old, nor a woman carrying a child before the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some wish to be treated, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there are many worms retained, so that the veins do not allow the intestinal waste to flow out and harm the main limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	does not heal who is too salted with foods, or drunk, to such an extent that he farts and urinates;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it is purged after a colic attack, vomiting, abdominal pain, excessive copulation with women, physical labor, staying awake and fasting, or any loss of vitality, either by something related to the weapon or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtle the humours, if it lacks size, with food and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter or bath, unless something prevents it, for the purpose of subtling the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein with the poison around the third, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself that day from work, pain, lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And let them be bound and comfortable, and let the lancer (surgical instrument) be higher than the one who is being treated, and scrape the arm 2 or 3 times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then gradually pull out the ligature above, for if it is too narrow or tight, the wound cannot heal without it.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then press the wound with your hands until the veins swell, and feel for them (the arteries).
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the lancer with a spoonful of old oil, then place your thumb on that vein under the joint where you want to treat it.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	The vein should not fail or break when piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like cords in a sieve, and some that are full of pus.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	If one applies heat, if it draws towards the fire and cannot open the vein, such is the case.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if (the patient) opens a vein, then the wound is too narrow; therefore, the surgeon should be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if (the patient) opens a vein the first time, that's good; if not, begin again under that place or immediately above it, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the vein is swollen, and the patient fears, let him rest for one day or two, and do not tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case of abscesses, let them wear shoes; do not enter water, then begin the incision if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the hole is small, or without subtle cautery you doubt that it does not bleed much as you see, trust in that same hole entirely with the direct flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Perform the work a little hastily, so that the flesh is inflamed; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not start the incision, and put a little oil of lard on it, for it soaks up the blood and is made in this place by the lard oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And so administer the oil ointment on every wound that you lance the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing makes them shrink and swell up, when it is placed on the wound; if it becomes too large, divide it into parts until it becomes smaller.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the lancing of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put a damp sponge soaked in vinegar and a little hot water on it, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it stays in place after several days without any black or green discoloration, it will not be harmful;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put something made of aloe or myrrh in boiling oil, mustard or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and signs of the abscess appear in the sanctuary: therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel the place soft when compressed by your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything above what we have said, for by chance in court without the artery; but make .i. a dry plaster to harden it, then cure it with another treatment until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; and if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and hollowed out, and has need of blood extraction, that you make a larger wound for him, and that the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to draw blood little by little, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bloodletting is safe from discharge of blood and damage to the nerve, and it is more effective than long bloodletting or wide bloodletting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs to be healed, it is necessary to give soft bread with grape pulp; if he has been scalded, drain the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is of cold constitution, eat soft bread in syrup before the healing, or syrup of honey with aromatic spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	If he has pus in the healing process, after the discharge of blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat and a fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open one of the arms and heal it again at times, if it is weakened by repeated bleeding, then let it heal little by little, according to the amount of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if you want to burst open one arm after the first bleeding and it has a strong chest, then let it heal for 6 hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if you want to heal from another part, it should be healed on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Since there is much blood within the body which has been heated, and it causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw a large quantity of blood, and to widen the opening as much as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Moreover, you will treat all conditions of healing, and place your hand on the toes when they heal, so that death does not come in their place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not good when you dislocate the arm, and make blood come out a second time, and the wounds are closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, you should extend the arm quickly, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until the blood comes out again; or you prick at the tip of the flame, as long as the frozen wound opens.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And place on it, i.e., a piece of linen soaked in hot water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is open, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has been pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If you need to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are connected to the vein of the head because they are composed of them.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient immerses his hand in hot water, until the flesh turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately, so that the vein is visible, then heal it with a cross, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the wounds wide, heal the junction of the hand well, and if it cannot be pierced, place the hand in hot water again, let the blood flow out into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is cold, do not push the hand into hot water, for it is put more in winter than summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, for there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the left-hand savary is good for all liver diseases, and this is how it works:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, push into hot water until the vein is inflamed, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the incision is transverse, and if you sew it up entirely, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for nerves are exposed below all the skin.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put the hand in hot water, so that the blood does not coagulate in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as necessary, put oil and wax on top of the vein to quickly seal it, and do the same with each one (vein).
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood from the left hand is useful for the sickness of paralysis, and do it as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood from the spine is useful for all diseases that are below the chest,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as diseases of the womb, and stopping of flowers, and sickness of the kidneys and thighs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its health is such that the patient should step into hot water, and rub over the vein until it perishes,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there are many rain-like drops.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	let the drop of blood therefore be as wide as possible or at the ankle, for it is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you let the blood flow from above the foot, beware of the veins that are below it, and let the blood flow through as when cutting; let the flame be quiet.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to start again, do so a little higher up, since the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the tendon of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The large vein of the sciatic nerve is at the shin bone, and its pain resembles that of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its pain is that the patient immerses himself or herself in water and pulls above the shin four fingers in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, you should drain it in every possible way, crossing over.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it heals as you cut it, for the vein is hidden, and it is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't pull it out [the arrow], no healing will come from that wound or the back of the foot, and turn towards the little finger;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make such a correction to the blood flow that you see, then undo the binding and put cotton on it and press; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by drawing blood or without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this blistering done without drawing blood has two methods: it is either by fire or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and blistering that is done by drawing blood and extraction has four parts in the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	The one is entirely on his head; and the others are under the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two more on each side of the neck; and the veins below the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the veins in the armpits; and the veins above the ankles.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the veins on each arm; and the veins on each leg.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the blisters on the two ankles; and the blistering does not involve blood, unless from small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	because of this you should not pierce it at all, as you do with venous bleeding.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered at all, neither with cold nor hot fire, in any disease that comes from swelling, until the entire body is emptied out.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity or custom it is necessary to bleed, we will administer it every hour at the beginning of the month or at the end, and morning and evening.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to fart, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who find distention and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness of the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, with their tongue swollen and spitting blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such [cases], who think, see by no blood and swelling and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, and especially during the month [of menstruation], we order to bleed after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The menstrual blood helps to relieve the headache... that comes from the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bleeding is in place of the menstrual flow
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not appropriate for someone of cold constitution or one who has scabs to use [the treatment], as this does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because the old and those with cold diseases should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And whoever heals themselves often become forgetful, and because of this it is necessary to place the leech (a tool used for bloodletting) a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The leeching at the neck is in the place of healing for the head and basilica (a term used to refer to a part of the skull), and therefore it is useful for treating the sicknesses.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and in cleaving of the channel of the throat, and to pierce, and to fill up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it must be pushed gently, for if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction or obstinacy of the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosations in the two ribs of the neck are worth the pains of the head, and obstruction, and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the place of the sanity of the basilica; and you must command the Lord that He extends His hand to perform it, so that He does not cut the artery and no flow of blood results.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations beneath the chin are useful for treating mouth disease and corruption of gums, as well as similar diseases in the mouth; they are located near the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for treating disease caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the ribs are as valuable as four veins in the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to be too deep, for the muscle is bare of flesh, and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the buttocks is effective for emordes from the root and for diseases beneath it, and it should be large and made of iron, as it needs to be well drawn; and in case it is too thin, it would break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses of the legs heal open wounds, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and remove pus; and they are in the place of the thighs and ankles, and in all cases they weaken the body over a long period, and bring phlegm in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the bladder (ventouse) is such that you first empty it, then fill it immediately and apply it hastily, move it equally, and not stop doing so until you see the place turn red and swell, and appear the redness of blood; then press and remove the bladders, and pay attention to the position of the body, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: you must pierce only once, and must make wide incisions, and a little deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the wound is large, you must pierce it twice: the first time to refine the blood vessel's path.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, you must pierce it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we should only do so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to draw much blood, we should often do so; and if the vein is thick, we should pierce it thoroughly, and the end should be tied off so that the arteries are punctured suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, you should anoint the joints of the armpits with sharp and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in fever, oil of watercress, or lilies, or chamomile, or anything similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take bitter almond oil or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person whom you are healing has thin flesh and narrow pores, do not put any oil on it,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash after the dislocation with rose water, or cold water, or marsh-mallow water, or cucumber water, or pearlwater, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from asafetida or marjoram and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great surplus [should] rise with old wine or grape juice, or the decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not advisable to let blood from a vein before the bath nor in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after venesection.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he purge himself, when he should let blood and when he has had blood let from him.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch the person who lets blood is choleric, and if he lacks it is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And cook peas, meat broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution, let him take honey syrup and fragrant mellow wine, which is between old and new, and eat apples and peas and small birds and young birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he will vomit, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give some men three times tracle or muskatel before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the wine be refined, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The boils that are placed to be struck are those that are placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, the abdomen and the buttocks, and the thighs, because these members cannot bear to be struck on them.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is not done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	As we put on the mameluke when the limb is unhealthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put vinegar on the belly and on the boil to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an abscess or arrow, using its attractive power by chance to draw out the abscess, or moving the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way is it done when placed on the spleen and the kidney when there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are administered empty to be sucked only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in cases of pleurisy and in this way the bladder is filled with hot water or water in which herbs such as comfrey have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister to be administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two fingers width and half a palm breadth in length, and have one small hole on its side, like pushing a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of iron, soaked before putting it on the member to prevent pricking the patient.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	have in the middle a rod of iron or steel, for placing a plaster (bandage).
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for boils on children are different than on adults, and on thin people than on fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this boil should be placed over the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the lancet or thread made of wax and place it across the boil where the rod is placed over the boil.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the bladder (ventouse) so it does not burn the patient
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member (limb), and your fingers should be on the perforation (pertus) that we have mentioned, so that when one sees, if steam goes out, then remove the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and press (apply pressure) on the lineament (area of injury) as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder (ventouse) which is administered in pleurisy disease, there should be no perforation (pertus), and it should not be administered with a needle unless when full of water, and it should only be placed on the member.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape: [This line doesn't contain a subject or verb, so it's not possible to provide an exact translation. The phrase "et c'est li forme" translates to "and this is the form" in English.]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction is not applied except to members where no bladders can be placed due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places. [Here the phrase "Sansues ne sont amenistrees" translates to "suction is not applied," "fuer que" means "except", and "en membres" translates to "to members".]
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in naked places of flesh, such as palms or soles, and other similar places. [The phrase "et en leus desnuez de char" translates to "and in naked places of flesh", "si com doi ou neis" means "such as palms or soles", and "et autres semblans" translates to "and other similar places".]
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are such that when you find sores in clean, sweet waters, you can take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in a nut in sweet water until they are rotten and have nothing inside;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then it should be purified with vinegar and wine, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the sores on top of it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they become swollen and hot, if it is a place where a blister can be applied, apply one, for it is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the limb and put it on a cushion, then sprinkle with warm water;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too far from the body of the blister, moisten one linen cloth with cold water and place it on top until the blister dries up.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are no open wounds, apply powdered glass or similar substances until it dries.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	And cover the area with half-boiled beans, leaving them until they harden, which will stop it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other sanguines (bloodletting agents).
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if bloodletting agents are not available, rub the area with fresh blood or insert an arrowhead until the blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they bleed.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see them bleeding, sprinkle a little of aloe and crushed seed or ash over it, then they will stop bleeding now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the repair of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Inform, dear son, that the foolish man abandons this chapter, he never saw any old books or read any letters from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, knowledge in our land is foreign, because I never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who have been proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	When fracture or dislocation or twisting or curvature comes to anyone, it is necessary that you treat the patient from both sides, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of the body, or infants, or elderly people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very hot, nor too cold; and do not eat cold meats, meaning cold joints, and boiled eye and shin meat, and drink no wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself excessively with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heating or spreading of matter to the member; if the patient returns to his former good government as he used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that cause thickening, or those that are viscous like cooked wheat in water and meat, and beef, and mutton, and veal, and fish, and fresh eggs, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For more frequent and quick healing of the bones, it is represented that nourishment is needed.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit cannot well recover or heal as their nature dictates due to the lack of strength of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But has no cure, reset on the broken bone, that is to say, large splints which bind and join the limb together, until it heals as it was before; and do not remove it completely from its work, and therefore feed it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of break in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to a tree, and another while sharpening, as the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, then it is a small fracture.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way it has its tool and appropriate instrument for restoration, according to what comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the fracture of bone is recognized by twisting and opening wide, and it sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when it has no twist or touch [the affected part], and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have a twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but put on the medicine that comes after this, and then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that are in the armpit, and the two dislocated parts, you should now adjust them equally, so that abscesses grow well.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses become hot, leave them for some days until the abscess is calm.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then make it equal to the muscles that you can easily and skillfully feel, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration where there are bones; then hold it as needed hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bones are broken in pieces, divide them into two parts, if it is hands or feet, or with your hand for small members, or with two ropes, or one rope and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you reset with all means the additions into their original position and ensure that your work does not cause pain or injury to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And align well the two shoulders of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems not to be well aligned: straighten it nicely, and do not strain or press it too much, nor make it hot and contracted like those who bring about abscesses and contractions in the member by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is set, punish the patient if he moves it, whether awake or asleep, turning, or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch carefully that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not properly set, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that it is set correctly, so that twisting does not come about when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be in various sizes and shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers, etc.: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and thin linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard cord, for the wide cords enclose the entire large member and tighten it equally on all sides, so there is no tear;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light bandages around them four times or five, according to the member, and tighten your hand a little on the cord, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, then move away from the break a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy joint, then take another ligament and turn it back right around the broken joint.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go to the part under the fracture and tighten it slightly, neither too strong nor too loosely, as we said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place pieces of linen or woolen cloth between the ligaments so they are all even, then tie it all up with one bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or boil, place something soothing on it and leave it for several days until it heals.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then bind your limbs with a strip of cloth or rope about half the size of a finger, or with a plank used for splitting logs, or with palm fronds, in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the bandage placed over the break be a little larger and thicker than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should be as long as necessary for the small or large limb.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold above the rafters just as you did at the first station, then tie above with a thread coming from below, as in the first station on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	Then tighten more above, but not too much; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who make their cords twisted with too thick flax, and that is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too thin; moreover, there should not be less than two fingers' space between each rafter.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has been struck by the heads of arrows in the shoulders after being reset, place linen or wool padding under them so they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the bone is shattered, I will explain the remedy below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, no need to apply hot iron rods before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of old plasters for restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour which is kept near the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method of the plaster restoring a break in various ways, and equally for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for restoring breaks, dislocations and twists: take aloe, linden, elder, asafetida, arabic gum and myrrh, all in equal parts; add aloeswood and mix with plenty of egg; if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones to their place, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for twisting: take mugat and vismalve, mix together 10; mirrhe and aloes, mix together 8; acaice 6; bolus armenic 10, grind well, and combine with vinegar or abundant egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for joints and dislocated bones, to soothe the pain that has arisen, and to treat it with cutting and breaking: take new linen, moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore [the bone], but it is good for soothing an abscess heat, and treating proper bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for plaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to hasten the healing of an abscess. Take root of comfrey, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of bean pods, of each one part; grind them and mix with wine, and when the members are scalded, mix it with coriander water or vinegar, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.
