Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger method of plaster when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of comfrey, flax seed, broom, lupine, and sage, flowers of violets and chamomile, from all one part; grind them and mix with vinegar or brine water, or wine, according to the warmth of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that no other substance should be put on a broken limb to restore it except for a plaster made of wax and oil, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it appears Galen says one should place dry, warm things on the broken limb to heal, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another remedy for injury and pain: take the mugwort plant and crushed human hair or bird feathers, and egg yolk, all evenly ground, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then let the plaster dry a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, or no rest is found or swelling occurs, hasten and dislocate it, and remove the splint immediately; then take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, dip in water, and lift up the place, until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, dampened in water or rose oil, and bind up a hot compress on top, until you are sure of the abscess being heated.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the inflammation of the limb should rest, and the pain be relieved, then resume the binding, but gently with a small amount of splint, and not too tight as before; and bind up until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is swollen and red and painful and inflamed, and you need to open it up and bind it, then repeat the process as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If no signs appear on the limb as we have said, do not undo it before 3, 4, or 5 days, and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the swelling subsides and the abscess approaches the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold it more tightly than before, and the flesh thickens as I said earlier; and if you see it dries out more than necessary, know that purulence cannot come in.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arise then from hot cold sweat, every time you dislocate it, and this should be done daily, and ease a little the ligament;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Then with this work, cut the swelling on the member and correct immediately what the foolish fool does, who leaves the member twisted: it is bad, and it is a dangerous thing to do, and I see nothing else but to tire oneself out and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures are, and various shapes, and their causes are defined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For fractures are made by sword blows, and the hilt strikes the bone all the way through to the point below the bone, as happens with a cleaver or fist; this type of fracture is called 'cleaving'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above piercing through, and this type of fracture is called 'complete'; and this is the break in the two types of bones, whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow from the side, a crack or a cut by a stone, falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent break, which approaches the membrane that lies beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is healed to the bone as subtle as hair, and it is small, therefore it is called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with stone, falling, or similar things, and causes the bone piece to enter within, and the fracture is closed as a blacksmith does when heating above a fire, then let the arrow penetrate it within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this occurs more often in those who have or a moist skull bone, as in the case of an infant's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens in all these ways of breakage that small fragments are dislocated, as is the case with bones; and I shall speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We should know all the ways of breakage by traction over them, and the inquiry with probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy resemblance is known by this: when the bone is exposed and scraped over it, if the break is blackened, it appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of the patient's conditions; and if you see any bad signs such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, high fever, hairs growing and turning red, or other signs in different positions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any uncertain signs, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the splinter first comes to you, and it is in winter, it should be removed before the fourteenth moon (which is about 28 days).
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is corrupted, and the complications mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches the tissue covering the brain, it is necessary to cut the broken part in such a way: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head, lift it up, and expose the bone in every possible way, and on the shape of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	If a flow of blood comes to reveal the bone or an abscess opens up, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And make the wound rest until the abscess subsides and bleeding is assured; then start to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two ways of work: the first way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made with iron instruments; and work lightly, so as not to cut the main part.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is forced and hard, then you must pierce it around, in such a way that you provide measurements with tapers, not making them so thick that they penetrate beyond the bone's edge, and above the point it should have a margin or circle, which doesn't allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have more than one, so each comes at the correct location on the bone's edge, so you have tapers for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one taper on the bone and turn your hand until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the taper slightly aside, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the fracture lines as subtly and lightly as possible, so that you draw the bone to your hand or any of the instruments that you have such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and trimmed, it is necessary that you reset the sharpness that is remaining of the bone with all other similar instruments resembling a cutter, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other cutters.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains anything of the small bones, no scales, gently remove them with instruments; then heal the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of work is the one that Galen mentioned, which is more sure; and he praised it much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the fracture opens up; so that when you have exposed this part, place beneath it the head of this incisor chisel, as shown in its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut through entirely, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently pierce the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is pierced to the bone, strike lightly, for one can break the bone senselessly and out of fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth, and the bone is only cracked from above, and there are small pieces, then one should smooth it out afterwards, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable amount in each place, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king [or leader] shaves his head closely first, then afterward with something more subtle, and does not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of haircut and breakage, it is necessary that you bring about the result according to his discretion; and this is not something that can be answered by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, it is necessary that you take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth doubled in 2 or 4 layers, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the wound, then provide another ligament, but do not tighten it more than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it remain for a day or two until the abscesses have calmed down, then release [the patient], and administer medicines like root of lilies, wheat flour, incense powder, Aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put on the wound, and immediately administer dependable medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	Keep the wound always clean, do not leave any ointment or bandage there, for when a linen cloth is applied to the brain tissue, it will corrupt and rot, causing great harm to the patient; for when something biting is put on it, it will cause pain from underneath.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no unfortunate accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with great uncertainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come violently except for medicine that we have put on it, which has this virtue, then you should take a part of honey and 3 parts of rose oil, and in glue, put one piece of linen, and lay it on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with methods of treatment as required, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but instead causes swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must press your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and insert the breakage inside the index finger, and to the pocket through the back, until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, you must insert a small stick into the nostril up to the root.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, repair it as such, and hurry to restore it within a day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If it is not in two parts, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then bind to the head of the needle threads of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Tie two threads of opposite parts, if the fracture is there; and let the threads be as thick as they fill the pores of the needle.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said any restorative that one should moisten the threads with butter, and to soften each day. I do not think it is good, but it should be moistened in a mixture of egg yolk and flour; then leave the thread, until the bone is hard, and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of goose are inserted in place of tendons, and if one layer of linen is around it, and the breakage is held, then blow the patient gently through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess comes to the opening as you are working on it, put beeswax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If an abscess does not come out, put plaster on the outside, made of wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light compresses on top, but do not bind the wound.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the neck is small, and it is broken into little pieces, pull them out with suitable instruments, then seal the wound with materials appropriate for that purpose, such as plasters and salves.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound within the neck, then treat it with bandages and apply planks of wood until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated below, and there is no wound outside, and only the break is visible, but it has not been broken in two, if one knows it easily, then it is recognizable as a corbel inside.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, place your index finger in the patient's mouth; if the break is on the left mandible, place your right index finger from outside and push it gently inside, and align it with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is displaced at two points, then you must administer an extension of two parts until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, hold them with a gold, silver or silk thread, then place a broken-baked mandible on top, and put on one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large and well-made stitch, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and attach it where you can, and command the patient to rest, and give him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure change (dislocate), dislocate it again on the third day, then reset it where it was dislocated; apply a plaster of milled powder with egg or flour of wheat, after removing the broken bone; and put on the plaster a light linen, and if the plaster sets and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; many times it heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when an abscess comes, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone when extracting it; use tools suitable for this purpose with caution.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it as necessary with fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces, if none remain, then sew up the wound, if it is wide, and apply one or more suitable dressing for healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the arm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force is broken many times towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated at two places, divided into parts, and is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the fracture is without wound, you shall have two helpers, so that one holds the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then align the fracture to your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and has neither appearance nor deviation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to stretch more, place a round bandage of cloth or linen around the patient's shoulder and make it thick as needed; then stretch and bind the force, and pull the bandage tight with your hand, aligning the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the dislocation from its enclosure because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side, and put a small pillow under his shoulder; and push the ministers (assistants) the shoulder downward until the bones of the dislocation are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find that it is broken, then it is necessary that you cut through it; and draw apart the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join due to any hindrance, strike one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the dislocation to keep it in place:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, not convex, and be of such a size as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, if you see, and one be wide, and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the abscess heat, if it opens, and if the wound is small, or you doubt about the abscess heat, then use linen cloths and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes from the abscess heat, then soak a linen cloth in rose oil, wormwood and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you place the plaster made of mill powder and egg yolk on top of the bone, and put light poultices under it, and place a splint under it if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then put on a double cloth padding and wrap it; then take a thin needle of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the needle through the break, and turn the bandage around the neck, and below the patient's jawbone, and below the sick person's jawbone; and pull from each side, and when you see that the fracture aligns properly, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then hold it every day, and when the swelling subsides, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his jaw while he sleeps to raise the shoulder; this will align the fracture by the alignment of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then start the treatment, if it is needed, and hold it steady and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and less in some cases.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is fractured or dislocated, it may not heal on its own, and only touch can be used to feel it; then set it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways that you can; then put flour from the mill with an abundance of egg and light bandages, and put two layers of cloth over it; then put a wide and thin splint, slightly larger than the shoulder, on top and make sure that under the splint there is no part of the shoulder protruding, if this happens use flax bandages to fill in the gap so that the splint fits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place and watch the wound every day; whenever it softens, bind it again, and make sure the splint is even if it has moved, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 30 days, and when this number is complete, remove the bandages, but be careful because it is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, raise it up, and cut the bone, and do as we have said in the treatment of an abscess to cool the heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with this method
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	Sometimes a limb is broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken within, it sinks downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of alignment, and immediately vomits blood, and the opening in the broken bone appears wide open, and it hurts a lot.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on their back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and carefully align it in all ways possible, so that the bone figure is as required; then place poultices and pouches filled with salt or another light substance on top of the broken bone, wrap it in one cloth, and attach it to the broken bone so that it does not move; then turn the limb round and round, and tighten it gradually, and check every hour whether the fracture has healed, and if it softens, tighten it again; and if it is necessary to dislocate it, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, you hasten, and dislocate it, remove the poultice, and direct those who have come for treatment; then reattach the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in large ones after the back and at the chest, and they bend only when they are slippery; and it is felt well by the examination of the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the repositioning is that you make it equal to the break, as necessary. Then put the splint, and hold it with a stick, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the broken rib is tilted inside, the patient feels intense pain and shortness of breath, like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces it; and he goes to points, and quickly vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and they have used great ingenuity for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the broken bone outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot compresses come, if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, let them be applied.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it was said by some that vents are placed on the wound to drain pus, and this seems reasonable; however, doubt exists whether the vents attract superfluous matter to the wound due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some said that the wound should be covered with damp linen dipped in hot oil and a tourniquet placed between the ribs to make it even; then it should be cured with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the broken bone and fear is present in the patient, it is necessary to make an incision over the broken rib, and it is necessary to put one instrument underneath for support; then you should cut the bone lightly, and pull it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if they are large, and dress it with plasters until it heals. And when abscesses come, place moistened linen soaked in rose oil on top, and on the broken rib; and treat the abscess over the broken rib while the rib is healing, and lie him down frequently on the side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a fracture of the bones in the neck, and so it happens with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take care if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that they are mortally ill in many positions, and if they do not speak or feel well when squeezed and pricked, know that the jointure of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will be healthy or not, take care if the feet are swollen, and if there is an accident involving the hands, and the back has sudden weakness and involuntary movement; and when it is brought onto the stomach, it still moves involuntarily. And when it is pressed on the back, it cannot be sat upon. Know that it is mortally ill: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to them, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you anoint it if there is an abscess burning, place oil of rosemary or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then put a comforting and drying plaster on top, bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, you should cover it with some oil; cut the bone, then join the two edges of the wound together with stitches if it is large, then heal it with healing ointment for as long as it is well; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," you should put your left thumb in its place and make it equal to the right hand, then apply a plaster and bandage on top if necessary; then bind it, and if there is any dislocation, correct it; and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it does happen, there is only slight reduction in pain at the site; it lasts for a long time, declines towards the opening, causes pain and swelling at the location where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and feel which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then equalize that break so it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of that break can be done.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it (the dislocation) straight, place the plaster on top, then place a stick or a splint over it, and hold the break still so that it does not move; and apply the joint underneath the ribs until the fracture is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess should burst, do not touch it until the abscess has healed, and place what we have previously mentioned on it; then return to the treatment, hold it as needed if there is no bad accident, and that's the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the chest and the neck of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a rod filled with coarse linen, in this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two limbs and the splints together with two ropes, and suspend them above; then place the patient on a chair; then lay the broken arm on the rod, until it reaches the correct position, and have a small amount of rod in between; then suspend it to a heavy object or the assistant holds it downward; then the healer puts the break in the correct position with both hands together, until the break returns as necessary.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that they restrain the patient on their bed, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants that one presses where it is broken with their hands, and the other presses all around completely, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the extraction is more forceful, then tie one cord below the break and above the break, and each attendant extends to their part. If the break is near the head of the shoulder, then put a medium cord below the buttock and another toward the back, both below the break; and similarly if the break is toward the back, then put a light cord without pressure until the break is level with the place, and with the back; then make it level, as required, and hold it, unless an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess comes out, do not hold it for more than seven hours, and put a soft cloth soaked in oil and linen on it until the abscess is calmed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you place the cestui (the instrument) on the break, then raise the arm toward the shoulder or chest; and tie the bandage and hold it on the shoulder and arm so that the arm is in a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint above the fracture, with one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it spans the fracture two inches from each side; then hold the splints in position, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, firmly and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the position of the splints and the strapping, as we have said, during the time when you are resetting the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then look at it every three days, to ensure that swelling or inflammation does not occur at the site, nor does pus come to the limb because it is too tight. Follow these instructions.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accidents occur, do not remove the splint for less than four days or more; let the patient rest on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; place one piece of linen cloth equally under the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or the strapping becomes loose; follow this instruction by the power of medicine, and give him the meat as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; when it begins to recover, it should be coarse. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within forty days of the whole thing; then it should be removed and a bath and ointments administered to the wound to heal it. If the incision is ugly and swollen, wait longer to remove it, up to one month.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius", of which one is small, and this one forms the little finger; and the other is large, and this one is below, near the little finger joint; sometimes only the larger ulna bone breaks, or only the smaller radius bone, and sometimes both.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the small ulna bone is broken, the restoration is easy and the healing; but when the large bone is broken, the healing is bad, and more difficult than when both bones are broken. If it is only the small ulnar bone that is broken, then it must be slightly extended, and aligned properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the larger bone that is broken, then it must be pulled more strongly; and extend it by one cubit, and raise the finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and the patient should cross himself on his own, and place a cushion in front of him higher than himself, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then stretch the assistants arms below to the part under his hand or one joint, and another assistant above. And then align the bones according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken in pieces, put each part back into its place, and if none of them can be properly set, cut off the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; take care of the wound.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If in the beginning of setting there are pus-filled sores, apply a thin cloth made of rosin and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; cover it subtly with one cloth until the sores have subsided. Then remove the rosin, and put the plaster of flour from the mill along with egg white on top, then place the splints; make sure that the splints at the site of the break are slightly longer and wider than the others. Remember that there should be seven or more splints in various positions: whether the break is in one bone or two. Tighten the splints more above the break than elsewhere, and do not loosen them for too long, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; ensure that the cloths covering the break are soft and moist, and neither hard nor rough; and let the threads, which secure it, be of linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And examine the member and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If any bad accidents happen to a member, such as itching that happens in a member, then you must irrigate the member with hot water until the itching is alleviated; and let the member not rest. Then begin the binding again, and if the ligaments are worn out and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the narrowing of the orifices cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you must soften it a little, and let it be for some days until the narrowing passes, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of the things that we have mentioned come to the patient, then do not loosen him for up to twenty days. Or if around that time, his hands go to his neck and his necks are equal, and he guards against movement and displacement, and sleeps on his back; know that this break is restored in thirty or forty days, and possibly in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture at the back of the hand and the fingers happens rarely, but it often occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient should lie with his back straight and evenly on the ground; then place his hand on a cloth stretched out, and the attendant should extend the broken bones and align them with mirrors so they are well joined; apply the plaster and bandages if an abscess does not form, then insert a splint according to the size of the fracture, and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the side of the palm near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to strap it to his fractured hand; then bind it with a long cloth, and make the splint as wide as the palm of the hand, and tighten it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the edge, it should be that you place a splint above, and another below in the heel, so that the hand remains open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and bandage the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, whether it is the thumb, it should be equalized as needed; and hold with the heel, and if you see that you place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not let it move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, equalize it, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in one place, for movement is worthless, or place a splint on top, such as a thumb; and take care in the healing and positioning of the abscess, and treat what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	broken ankle
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and it is clearly seen when it twists forward and backward; and the restoration is as follows: one ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his ligament equally to its place; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the break is near the root of the thigh, one ligament should be towards the shin, and the other ligaments below the break. And if it is near the knee, then the ligaments should be located at the knee, and the extension should be down; then adjust the bone with both hands so that it is in its natural shape, and then apply the splint, and bind it, unless pus comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should bend the leg upwards, bind it firmly in two or three layers, and leave the excess material outside. Then rotate the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, put one long pin between the thigh and the leg below the knee, remove the knee cap, and bring the tip of the pin above; then rotate the leg upwards on both the leg and the thigh, bind the splint again, and place a splint over the bone of the leg; then use woolen fabric to make the binding equal around the area where the leg is bound, then start tying four or five turns around the splint. As you progress higher on the splint, loosen the binding. Take the two pins that you inserted between the leg and thigh, bind four more splints over them, then go back to the bottom of the pin, dislocate it if necessary so it doesn't move from its place, leave it like that; there should not be any abscess or swelling, or other such things.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a fracture, straighten it and align what comes out, as we have said many times; if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be cut off if possible; if not, the area should be broken and the fragments removed; treat it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way as if iron stakes are inserted into it, just like the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration, this does not alarm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thigh is restored within one day, or a little more or less, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin area
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the groin area there are few breaks, but it dislocates many times. And if it breaks, it is not only a fracture, but rather a fissure or rupture, and it involves all wounds, has pain, and this is felt very much.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes that which is rounded at its joints until it can be moved assembled; then place the splint, and put in a round peg, if you need it, and tighten it as needed, then check all the arrangements we have said in other breaks, such as abscesses, boils, and other similar ones; put at each accident that which is needed for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that the leg has two bones, of which one is called "the humerus" directly and the other "the radius"; and it happens just as a fracture in the arm occurs, and therefore the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	If the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it turns underneath. Then apply traction, make it straight, and tie the splints equally; but if the fracture is misaligned or has multiple pieces, the traction should be less and lighter, and align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two fists full of straw that will brace the leg on one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in a knot so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should administer one bandage of straw for the length of the leg, and it should be tied together, and the leg will be immobilized for movement, and properly made at the break where there is injury; move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident; heal it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breakage, but the bones of the foot sometimes have a break and the toes may be broken, and there is no fear but they are crushed in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bone of the foot, and you see one bone rise above the other, then place the patient on his back as if he wanted to walk, and then place your foot on the patient's stomach where the bones are elevated, and press as much as necessary until they return to their places; then place a splint and padding on it, and place a small board with two flat cups under the affected foot, then pull the bandages around it, and do other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after four or five days have passed, undo the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, either fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if either of the bones is fractured, restore it as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the fractured bone according to its length, and it should be slightly wider; then place under it the board that I mentioned, and pull it towards the fracture site; and if there are two or more fractures, break them, placing a splint on each fracture, wrapped in one linen cloth, and secure the board under the foot; and ensure that the top of the board is facing the abdomen of the foot, covering it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have said; and treat each accident according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the female bone is broken, let her sit with her thighs apart, then incline her to the back part and hold her from behind; then fill the hollow of the nature (pelvis) with cotton, and put as much as a large stone in it; then spread her legs, and lift up the buttocks little by little, and push the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the nature (vagina), and the bone returns with the stone; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of a goat, and tie a string to it, and push the entire bladder into the nature; then blow into the string forcefully, so that the bladder inflates within: the nature will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days until it is healed.
