Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the thumb (for man or woman) is broken, restore it as we have said in the "humerus"; and these breaks should not be hidden from him who puts his study and skill to use regarding them and pays attention to my book. For the fractures signify many different ways of restoration: therefore, take note.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the arm into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with an open wound, whether it is large or not, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, that it should be set now, as the testimonies of the healings that we have mentioned show.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then apply vitriol to it, if you have nothing else; then begin to set the fracture in that same hour, or continue on that day, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses arise, wait until the ninth day, allowing them to be pacified, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad event.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed at the surface of the wound, it should be set gently with light pressure and in a slightly extended position.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the tendons are not prepared for setting in an equal position to your hands, you must align it with this tool made of iron, which is 7 or 8 inches long and the width is according to the size of the wound; therefore, the mirror should grasp 3 or 4 fingers, according to what is needed in each bone-setting procedure; and let it be round and somewhat large so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and sharp at the front and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche", which means that the curved bones should be placed on top of the bone's exposed surface; then push it once until it returns to its original position and align them with each other. If the fracture is subtle, and the tool cannot firmly grasp the bone, it may be necessary to cut the bone's tip, so that the tool can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, within your power; then remove that which is immobile in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do what is necessary until it is in its proper place, then moisten one linen cloth in black stitching vinegar, and clean it properly if it is summer; do not put any oiled cloth or other substance on the wound, which would cause rot and corruption; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound open, and cover the surrounding area, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not tightened with a fracture; and many times have foolish surgeons done this, and have caused either death or rot for the patient, and may the bandages be softer and more pliable than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is large or bad and you fear that there may be a mishap, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, do not apply ointments; but wrap around it, instead of ointments, hard linen cloths and bind them. And after one day or two, if you see swelling at the wound, remove what you had placed on it and put on healing balms such as tetraformula and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be set straight in this manner so that the bones are aligned lightly downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but instead bows back, since there are small pieces of bone, therefore you must try to open the wound and remove all the loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula or some other form of corruption occurs, you must treat it according to what is mentioned in the previous chapter. When the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh bone or shoulder bone, or similar large bones, do not drain it, for many times death may come; however, leave it until it can be drained; perhaps it will heal by itself after twenty days or thirty. Then, if you can, cure the wound; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises on the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Often times after the breaking of health, especially near the joint, it is a horrible sight to see the figure of the limb; and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then of yourself: if we are to administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocola, acacia, and similar others, in such a way that you take one of these things or all together and crush them with sharp wine or with vinegar or egg white; and put it on the sore in poultices, and press it well, and do not remove it for many days; then you dislocate it, and repeat another, as long as the nodulation is removed; or you strain over a piece of plank well made; because the property of the plank is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the nodation has already become hard like stone, and it needs to be removed, you chop it off, and make the superfluity apparent; or you shave it with a sharp razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and remains after the members are weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one of them being that it was tied too tightly and not as needed; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive arrows; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body become thin, until the blood multiplies in him; then administer a bath, and give him joy and pleasure; afterwards put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nutrients to it, and the sore often gets hot with cold water, until the nutrients reach the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration and the bones broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless its natural function does not perish; do not believe the foolish who say one must break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and it brings great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and tortures are fresh, then they should be soothed with hot water or softening herbs such as comfrey leaves, radishes, medicks, and similar things; also, make a poultice of mollifying medicines such as daqiu, and take musk from the comfrey plant, mix it with gum elm or sesame oil, and apply a poultice; or you may take ripe figs, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the node is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands. Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is growing and hardening, as stone, it requires to be cauterized, it should be covered up to the bone, making a subtle incision gently; and place moss and cotton in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it is now necessary to return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joint swells, and perhaps it can be reset to its place; therefore, it is not advisable to move it until the hour when it has subsided: many times it causes pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Furthermore, when this occurs, you should clean the patient, then let it rest until all abscesses have subsided; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset the dislocation, and heal each member according to its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the neck down to the feet.
des mandibules	The jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated from their places, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are somewhat disjointed from their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and causing the saliva to flow out of the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns by various means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully developed, you must quickly reset it, without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and presses one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be spread out, to make it even; and instructs the patient to soften, his lower jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the hand is made even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, it is the same if it is both lower jaws together, you anoint them with hot water and oil, until they are easily reset; do not rush to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset equally, the patient's mouth should be closed and warm oil and wax paste (balm) applied to cover it lightly with many threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on his back, with his arms between two pillows so that they do not move to either side nor make an effort to move, but he should take light meat until the pain subsides, and his jaws should be tied.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he should eat lightly as he wishes but not strain himself in opening the mouth to eat or drink until the jaws are bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set right again within an hour and are not returned to their places, fever and common sweats come, and possibly abdominal rupture, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times he who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate inside the ribcage due to continuity and pain, and it is occasionally dislocated outward, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back and extends his arms; then presses the joint with your palm and it will return; then put on the traction device (emphaustrum) and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the shoulder that is facing towards the side cannot be dislocated; if it can, and if it occasionally dislocates, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the traction device (emphaustrum) and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, the head of the shoulder is returned when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only four ways: one is when it dislocates at the socket below; and the second is at the hip part; and occasionally dislocates above, but this rarely happens.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside through the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the socket, particularly in those with little flesh, for they can easily dislocate it; but in those with enough flesh, it dislocates little, and returns little.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, a blow or fracture occurs, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it, as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	Dislocation is known when it is turned towards the socket, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find obvious differences between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find in the shoulder blade a hollow, and under it press gently on the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot return their hand to its place, nor make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And if it is dislocated upwards, do not cover it up, for you can verify it by pressing on it;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister raises the patient's hand high, then places his palms underneath it, and forces the joint upwards to its place; and the minister raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it down; it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said in hands for several days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring him a soothing and comforting salve, such as a decotion of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and give it to him.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then lay the patient on his back, and place an equal piece of linen under it, neither too soft nor too hard, then the physician should put his foot on the linen, and correctly pull the head of the shoulder out, and pull the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister ties down the head of the patient so it does not move forward; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that you can reset it in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be present one man who is larger than the patient; and be straight towards the cost side, and push the shoulder under the patient's armpit, and raise the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs on a rope.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister pulls the hand of the patient towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, then take some weighty thing with him, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also reset in another way: and it is one long needle that is inserted into the ground, such that the head of the shoulder is as round as a pea, and not too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft linen over it, and the patient should be standing upright; then his hand on the other side should be stretched out in a form, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return with all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment: take a needle of two hands width long and four fingers wide, which has a rounded head for entering deeply under the joint, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the patient on the bed with a soft pillow beneath, so as not to hurt him, then place the patient's shoulder under the patient's armpit; extend one arm above the post, and hold the dislocated shoulder above the post, and the arm near the wrist to the patient's head, then place another arm on one side of a broad beam of a door, and let the hands hang down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side; the joint will then be put back in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, you must put an equal-sized cloth under the armpit, then sprinkle the splint prepared with mill powder, along with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around it, then tighten the bandage under the armpit accordingly, and twist the cord over the splint, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be fed a little amount of food, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then feed more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it remains firm and does not become soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of its place due to moisture or for another reason, then you must administer three cauteries as stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place and cannot lift the arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either compressed or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the hip, and the buttocks or backside, is caused by impact and stretching of hands, and another treatment may be applied; and care should be taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing of the member comes swelling, and it moves slowly, then let the patient use baths many times, until that swelling subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The cost of dislocation is...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocation of joints costs [to] be dislocated at points, and it costs [to] return to its place; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, and both before and behind, and the dislocations are not repaired because it is clearly seen and felt; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the diseased joint with the healthy one, then it can be seen clearly. For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset [the dislocation] thus when abscesses come, for if abscesses come, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be set back into place entirely, especially when it is at the rear; it is worth more than other dislocations, and it is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes there.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you stretch out your hand to your two hands; and the arms should be spread out, and the hands should be placed on the mirror according to the outline around it, above and below, and push the joint to its sockets or root of the palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it will return when you fold your hand over your hand and push from the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong traction; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they mark it with two ministers, so that it does not move during traction; then turn the arm on both sides, then when you have wrapped a double large cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, oil it to soften the jointure, then push the jointure firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put dry plaster with egg on it and hold it firmly, and wrap the arm around the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is in its place, break the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the manipulation and the ligament, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if there is pain after the repositioning of the joint and it becomes swollen, bathe and rub it well and press until it is soothed; or place a woolen bandage around the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it weeps, rub the joint gently, then place the bandage back on, and then enter into a bath; and do this 2 or 3 times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moist sheep's wool with butter on it, and hold it in place; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the wrist is light, more so than other joints; it should be returned to its place quickly, immediately when it is dislocated, unless the limb is swollen or there is hot abscess nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the repositioning is that you place the affected hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand, and align the mirror so it matches, with the palm facing the appearance of the jointure, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Therefore, you must make sure it is in the right place; then the patient should place the back of their hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on the table, and make the affected person put their other hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply a plaster to soothe and heal the abscesses, and let it remain in this way until it begins to improve.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if the person cannot tolerate it and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the dislocated joint remains displaced.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And the patient must not feel heat except as long as his hand is paralyzed and cannot grasp anything: therefore know that the nerves are cut or the arteries; there is no other means of healing but to tighten with fire cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else has value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, place the plaster that we have said upon it, then press and leave for five days, then release and leave so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well and there is no swelling, wet with hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers on the hand are occasionally dislocated from both sides, occasionally at the back of the palm or the front.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then bend the finger and push the dislocation towards your palm until it returns, then hold the finger's head and turn it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and leave it for two days, then equalize it on the third day; and bind it, as we have said, and loosen it from time to time, make it move, and tie it again; do this frequently until it is straight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And similarly do [the same], if it is dislocated in the abdomen of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do when it is dislocated from another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	for the dislocation of the vertebrae of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebrae of the back or neck are dislocated, if there is no cure for it, then death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that excretions leap out involuntarily, they cannot be held in, and many times the limbs become swollen, such as the two legs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the spinal column moves at four parts; that which moves towards the back is called "gibbosity".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure is that you check if gibbosity has come from childhood; if there is no remedy or healing from it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old ways of healing used to be spoken of in grand words, but it has not proven to be of great benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	However, I have shortened (abridged) it according to my intention and have created instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gland (or swelling) which comes before, there is no remedy nor health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and the same one that comes directly in two sides, and there is no cure for it except the one that comes at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be extended on his face in one even position, and have pressure under him to prevent him from bleeding;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert one pin into the head of the patient in the ground and another at the feet, and tie a rope around the ankles, thighs, knees, and shins of the patient;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers know the ligaments, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the four tendons;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well closed, the tendons as we have said, and the mirror place his hands on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a board four arms long and rounded at the bottom, and place the patient on his side, and push the end of the board under the bottom, then put the middle part of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And place the mirror's feet on the other end of the board and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not, use the wheel that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you insert two splinters into the head of the patient's large arm and towards the joints of two others, and between each splinter, inside and out, a palm-width space.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And in each splinter, there should be a pin, or a turning key, and the splinters should be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move; and between two splinters should be another splinter rotating, like keys, and in two rotating splinters, there should be two small pins of a palm-width length to turn the dislocated joint.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the rope that is among the joints to the dislocated joint toward the head, and another rope toward the joint at the other dislocation, and each of the servants turns their dislocated joint with all the rope, and the master sets the splinter equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a drying plaster on it with abundant egg, then bandage it, and then apply a hot iron rod of three fingers in length, which penetrates the area of swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a rope, as we have said, and use the patient with gentle heat until it is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines along with the iron rod as we have said before; and sometimes a splint is also used.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes the appearance comes at the back of the spine, and it is believed to be dislocation; but this is the bone that opens, so one should not make any presumptions; for by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Note that dislocations of the shoulder and the joints of the arm only come from dislocations, and not in other joints; and the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, front and back; more on the inside, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when the sick joint (shoulder) is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee at the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the loosened shoulder joint that becomes inflamed from abscesses due to this cause, because the hip joint comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens to swell, is that this incident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose leg is swollen, are that it is straight according to the completion; however, it does not double at the knee due to pain, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot do so beforehand, and it retains its urine, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose back hurts, are that he cannot stretch his knee or bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the hip is located under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The corrections for this type of dislocation are as follows: examine if the dislocation is old and remains in its position without treatment; and there should be no presumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of fresh dislocation, which is of four types of dislocations, you should act quickly by turning the joint and pushing it inward and outward, and move it left and right; if it returns, it will not need any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	If it does not return in this manner, then you should call upon one strong minister and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie a rope around the thigh.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he presses his hands beneath the buttocks, then tightens a rope-like thing on the calf; and another grasps the head of the rope.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And they all extend upwards and downwards at the same time, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If the shoulder is not dislocated, treatment for its similarity is required. When the dislocation is at the front, you should remember to elevate the patient on his unaffected side, then place the rope around the root of the thigh and the joint that is beneath the armpit, then pull the rope upward towards the armpit and towards the shoulder;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant by the hands and embrace the swollen thigh of the affected shoulder, and stretch it out forward in this manner: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot fix it in this manner as we have said, then you must tie the two legs of the patient together with a strong rope above the heels and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two feet more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then let him be suspended by a rope around his neck and above the ground there should be two long arms; then instruct one servant to embrace the thigh, and another servant holding with the patient, who will hold the thigh in place, for the joint is coming back quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is on the outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in that which has swollen up, and draw one cord around the sick leg properly, and also around the thigh.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then place two cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one cord between the thighs in the patient's groin area;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And place moist cloths around it to prevent the patient from bleeding, then extend each of the limbs towards him, and with one hand equalize the dislocation for the other.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that is good. If not, place him on a table, press as we have said in the swelling, and lie the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as quickly as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the hand on the sick angle, then press with the other hand, and move it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it should not be extended downward nor raised above ground, instead, it should be as if the patient were lying on a bed with both shoulders dislocated, as we have said in the treatment of double-shouldered patients.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and lie on his back, and the limb should be extended as we have said before, and it must press against the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and when the patient extends his legs and they are even, then adjust the knees, place the splint, and bind with a strap so that the shoulder does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And it rests for three or four days, then dislocate it, place a splint on it; and if you see that they are even, hold steady as before, and let it be. For three days; then dislocate it again, and make it walk well, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee joint is dislocated in three ways: inside and outward, behind; do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, understand that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his front side, and place his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee with your palms, and pull it between your hands, then fold the two sides of the knee in half; and another servant extends his foot until the knees return to their place, and the signs are that it bends his leg at his knee easily.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And apply the plaster on it, and make the leg straight to the thigh, and bind them together tightly for 3 or 4 days, then release; and do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not straight, administer strong traction, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs show that the ankle is swollen, and it tends forward towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is slight, and it should be done gently when only crushed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is fully dislocated, you must have the patient sit straight and hold two assistants on the leg above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot upward firmly.
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	And do this twice as we said, pulling and pushing the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start over, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it still cannot return in this way, place the patient on his back on the ground and make a firm hole in the ground between his knees, and tie strips of cloth around so that the patient does not bleed.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the ministers mark the thigh, and another minister extends the leg to his hands or to the first joint, so that he lies on top of the leg's neck;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Each minister extends equally, and the patient should remain between the thighs of the ministers to hold the patient when stretching him.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then the doctors equalize the dislocation in their hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below it, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, put the plaster and cotton on it, and press firmly, tie the leg to the thigh, and watch the nerves that are above the calf, so that the ligatures are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the ligaments soften, hold them tight; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and make the patient walk for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it goes past that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess has come, it is necessary that you appease it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	The two (hands/arms)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the limbs are dislocated, they must be very carefully extended without any effort, and it is an easy matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or the thighs, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or table upright and place your foot against that part where the jointure opens. Then press firmly with your foot until it goes back into its original position.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is leveled and there is no gap, if you place a table with two legs under the sole of your foot, press firmly on it, leave it for four hours, then release it, and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and patient, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and first use soothing ointments for abscesses that are hot, and leave the patient in the hands of God if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess heals.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer things that soothe the abscess, and treat the wound, as needed, with hot poultices.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	If with the dislocation there is a fracture and small bones are displaced, fix them, and do as we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And keep away from entering into fear, as I have said, for it will harm you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arms and body. Amen
Explicit le romen de fisique	Translation: The end of physics
